O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O ye, dear sons of mine, I have completed this book, which is the last part of the art of medicine with its prescriptions and explanations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I should complete this treatise with this text, which is part of the work on hands, that is to say "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And since the work on hands is well-established in our region and is deeply rooted in all matters, it is a perfection of knowledge and capability, and there is no delay in its application but only small descriptions in books by the ancient ones that the hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this has come error and vanity, and intentions are closed and knowledge is distant.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	And it seems to me that I should revive this treatise with the arrangement of this text according to the method of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and I will come with the forms of the tools for cauterization, and other instruments for the work, with the adjustment of the declaration and preparation of them, as is fitting.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because no good master of hands is found in our time, the art of medicine is neglected.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And he who engages in this should master the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so that he knows the judgment of the limbs, and their shapes and connections and separations of bones, and has knowledge of the osses and nerves and joints and the number of bones, and the movement and flowing of veins and the rest and the source of their movement.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And for this reason it is said by Hippocrates that with work there is no lack and with rest there is little; and especially in the art of the hands.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you at the beginning of this book that if someone is not knowledgeable about the things mentioned above, he should be careful so that he does not make a mistake and harm people; so that I have wanted many times to prevent those who engage in this science from doing so, because they abandon their knowledge and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	I saw a foolish man who cut an abscess on the neck of a woman, and he also cut the arteries in her neck; so much blood flowed that the woman died in his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And I saw another foolish man who tried to remove a stone from a man's bladder; the stone was large; he brought away a piece of the bladder and the man died in three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I have also seen a man who was called to remove it, and saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone; and if he tried to remove it, he would surely die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another foolish man who took as his cure an earl of our land who had a broken leg, and with the breaking there was a wound; and this ignorant healer pulled out the break on top of the wound with great effort, leaving no scar on the wound, and left it like that; and he commanded that it should not be taken off; and it delayed so that his leg became completely gangrened and his foot came to destruction.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to go to him, and I hurried to come to take off his leg; and when I took it off he was at peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But all the ways that the member was corrupted were already confirmed, and it could not be healed; and the corruption did not cease to go by the member as long as the members were completely lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another mirage that broke out into an abscess with a putrid taste, and then inflamed by the evil of its dignity.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For leprosy, when it is purulent with melancholy humor, does not come but one must touch it with iron if it is in a good place so that one can take away all that is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And because, small children, you must know that the work of hands is divided into two divisions: namely, work in which there is danger in many conditions; and I will show in each of these books where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	For since it is necessary that you keep them, so that the bad smell cannot offend you. If you take your weapons in agreement, and attack your enemies lightly and firmly, and use the best way, so that through the grace of God you come to salvation and are healed; and leave the probable disease of grief health; and hold your weapons away from what makes you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you can come from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galien gives some advice: "Do not take on the care of a bad disease, lest you be called a madman.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapters are about fire cautery and water-based medicine, and the next chapters deal with the order of the process step by step, as well as the forms of the instruments, the fierms of cauterization, and all that is necessary in this work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapters deal with the handling of hair and nails, suction cups, wounds, arrow extractions, stones, and similar matters; and the third chapter discusses the organization and forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter deals with restoring dislocations and twists, and similar matters; and it is ordered that the bones be broken just as much as needed, and the forms of instruments are described.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Therefore, since we remember the work, it is necessary that I describe the quality of the aid and the harm of each color.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of the aid and the harm is the longest word and subtle science, and the replies to this are agreed upon by many sages; and I am short on words because I reduce the length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that fire is an aid for all colors in which there is matter, except for two types of color: namely, hot colors with dry matter, and cold colors with dry matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In hot and dry matter together, they all agree and say that cauterization is great help; and the other said the opposite: that cautery is no aid to illness that comes from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire if it is hot, and should not be cured by hot disease from heat or dryness; and he who says the opposite that cauterization does great help to hot and dry illness that comes in courses of people.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of the man and his moisture to the complexion of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have not found it once by experiment.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And all way, no force should be used but by him who has experienced it, and who knows through long use the chapstick of cauterization, and the diversity of complexions in men, their dispositions and causes of their illnesses, and the places and spaces of the ten; otherwise we have no fear even for cold and moist illnesses.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all of this will agree with and correspond to the fire cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, children, that fire cautery heals together if there are secretions from wounds, and with greater goodness than medicinal fire cautery.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and comes only to the member that is burned, and does not harm another member in any way.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The burning medicines come from one member to another by removing, and bring about disease of great healing; and perhaps fire due to its height and the goodness of its substance does not do this, unless there is surplus.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	I have found this by experience and from the long service and study that I have put into this art, and it is based on the truth of things; and so, I beg your pardon for the length of my words, for I do not like to deny you the secret which is hidden in fire, and the quality of the work, how it drives away the diseases of the body, as the philosopher says by way of proof; and take it into consideration.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that these cauterizations should be made at what time; they are to be prayed over.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cauterization is appropriate at all times, for since the resulting harm can be prevented by the aid of cauterization; more so, the cauterization is done for necessary and urgent pains that cannot wait for the time when greater harm may come to the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And I do not think at all, dear son, as they do so foolishly; for with the disease that is cured by cauterization has no return; and it serves thus: but it is not so as they believe, since cauterization is only medicine that changes the complexion, and dries up the humors which are the cause of pain, and is worth more as a medicine because of its quick action, and due to its virtue and its nobility.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And it is possible that the disease comes according to the complexion of the sick and the place of the disease and its virtue; and superfluities are gathered in him by the acquisition of flesh and similar things, unless cauterizes are administered at the place where there is a little superfluity and moisture, as cauterizes of thick for pain, and similar things, and the like pain does not return; but it happened little.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why the cauterizes are called the derriers of medicine, and that is to be seen; but they do not believe that the cauterizes are worth after medicine, but their intentions are wrong, and the cauterizes are the derriers of medicine because when we administer ways of cure in any disease and they do not work, then we administer the cauterize, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore, open well that the cauterizes are the derriers of medicine, not at all according to the intentions of foolish men.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	Li ancien dirent que cauteres d'estrument d'or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l'or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n'est mie voir car je l'ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c'est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d'or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	The ancient ones said that gold cauterization instruments are less prone to inflammation than those of iron, and they only mentioned the color of gold and its high purity for these qualities; they said that the heat of gold cauterization instruments does not cause inflammation, but this is not true, because I have tried it, and I found that it is true in some people; and gold cauterization instruments are more beneficial than those of iron, as they say. However, when you heat up a gold instrument, it doesn't take long to cool down; and if you heat it too much, it will catch fire, and this is enough to prevent it from being used.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And so we use our fire cautery, which we have prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or you should read this chapter to the end, because then the vision will be clearer.
dou cautere olivaire	The olive oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	The olive oil cautery is useful for moisture and cold on the skull, and because of many humors that descend from the hairs, and the ears, and for many dreams and pain in the teeth and throat, and most especially for all the illnesses that come from cold such as paralysis and lameness and apoplexy and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The shape of this cautery is such that the patient should be cleansed with a solu
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then place the crossbow in your hands, and place his hands on his pelvis; after that, put the root of your palm on the root of his penis between his two roots; and let where your two sides come together, so that it bleeds from there then heat the fire which is called "olivare", by which this is formed:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it on the sigil of ink, and make it descend and extract your hand little by little in turning; then release your hand separately, and burn the root where you see the bone I small; and if you do not see it, so start the fire again as soon as you see the bone, as I told you; after that, take a piece of rope, and put soft cotton inside, and put on the sigil, and let it be III days; after that, put wet cotton on butter; and leave it until it is burned; after that, treat the wound with the ointment which is called "tetrafarmaçon", until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And they said that the older ones, the more the wound is open, the more it will spew; and for this reason if you move it.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they said that no one should let the burn last so long that part of the bone is burned, and then cut off what is burned from the bone, and be cured.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And the other said that one must let the burn last so long, and squeeze it with such force that the humor comes out as wide as a woman puts it in her vagina so that the humors come out; and one must let the wound be open for a long time; after which one must cure and heal.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two ways of burning seem to me neither good nor bad in all respects except that they may be dangerous for certain people; and it seems to me that I should let them burn because the joint is weakened by continuous solutions of nature, as we see with other limbs; and even if the joint of the patient is weak by nature, and the first appearance of the cautery seems to me more safe and gentle, and from this one I act in such a way that it is salutary.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the child's pain in the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When all over the head comes chronic pain, and lasts a long time, then use yarrow and pills which are called "cochie", and cleansing of the head and oils and poultices; and if one does the cauterization that we have said above, and it doesn't help.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care that the patient is of strong nature, and is not too cold; then cauterize it a little as we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After doing the cauterization on each corner of the head up to the bone, as we have said above, and do the cauterization at the place which is called "vasselz"; and put the cupping glasses; and hold your hand so that you do not see up to the bone: the patient feels too much pain in this cauterization than in the others, and I will speak about it later; and it comes that the cauterizations of the corners are thinner than those by which one cauterizes the middle part of the head, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	Dou cautere dou cheif
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When suddenly in one part of the chief comes pain up to the oil, and the head is extended by medicines of this world, and other cures have been made as I said in the division of diseases, and none has benefited: then do cauterize according to two ways, that is to say, of medicine water and of fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cauterization of medicine water if you squeeze a bit of ale, and scrape off the bark and wrap it around the joint, and then make the temple or place where the pain is in a little way that you can reply the ale to remove the skin; and when it has been replied so you bind it well and leave it there for twelve hours; and then unbind it and treat with garlic oil, and leave the wound for two or three days; then put cotton dipped in balm until it can heal.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the cure of wounds as long as he is well; and if you see fit to use any of the burning medicines that I have written or prescribed in the treatment of burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The fire cautery if it is according to this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cauterizer so that it is hot:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And call it "clos" for as the head is made in the form of a hole or he has I piece of corbeure, and at the center to a small appearance; and put it on the painful place, and hold your hand and turn the fire a little slightly, until the half of the wound is burned; and release your hand so that the artery does not burn, which is faster, and runs abundance of blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After put cotton in silk, and put it on the place for III days; then I put cotton wet in butter, and then heal the wound with the cure of wounds as long as he is well; and if you want to cauterize this headache with the cauterizer that is called "cultellare", all over the tip, and be careful not to cover the artery in this headache which is not old.
de emigraine	of headache
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you treat headache as we have said before in the division of diseases, and do not profit from it, and see that the cauterization mentioned above does not suit it, then it is necessary that you heat the cautery called "cultellare" until it is white; and sign thus over the hurting place a line of half an inch long, and lift your hand once, and hold it so that you do not cover the artery and do not come to the bone; and guard against the jaw that mutates when you drink, and let the rest be done in the middle way; but I will tell you how to stop headache when the artery is cut, and I will show you at what place it affects in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that these caутers do not suffice to the illness, and the patient suffers, cauterize him at the top of the head as well as we have said, and cure the wound until it is healed; and if you see, administer the caутer which we have said or chapistry of the extraction of the artery, with the caутer that has II knives; and this caúters are better than that and more aiding.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of the pain of ears from cold weather
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain in the ears comes from cold weather, and medicine and other treatments that we have spoken of in the chapter on healing are applied, but the pain does not stop, then heat this caúter called "poins", of which the form is:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait X poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After applying the "poins" caúters all around the ear that hurts, or around both ears where the pain is felt at the root of the ear, and then move away from the ear's root a little so as not to touch it; make X points around each ear; after that heal the area until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	of the torture of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	is cured by fire only of those that move with flu, as we have said in the division of diseases; and do not make fire on similar things that come from scabs and lice of hair.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you cure this torture of the mouth that moves with fluid, scabs, and lice, and this is not worth it, then you must cauterize the patient with three cauterizations: one in the root of the ear, another a little further away from the temple, and the third at the junction of the two lips; place the fire on the part that should be healed, and let half of the burn be completed before removing it. And this is the form of the fire:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And is the appearance of the cutting that we have placed before, but it is a little more subtle and it is necessary that the knife is a little thicker; after healing the place as I said before, as long as he is healthy.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is old and you treat it like we said before, it does not benefit, and the patient does not have a fever, then do IIII cauterizations: II on the II horns of the head, and I cut the head off, and I cut the vasculus as we said before, and the cauterization on the mouth of the stomach; and let it heal like we said before.
de litargie	of tar
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this disease, it is necessary to give the patient many years and pilules of vinegar in the head; after re-cutting the head of the patient completely, and placing on the occiput the plaster of mustard which is written or treated with plasters; and this is the way of cauterizing: if you do so as I said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If it is healthy then it is good; and if it is not, he should make three fire cauterizations on the head at the top of the neck, with a space of two inches between each one; and the doctor as for the others, and if you see him writhing, and the patient suffers, he should make one cauterization in the middle; and it is a trade, two others on the two horns, and the doctor until it is healthy; and the cauterizations that are called "olive", as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	The head should be washed with water and with what we have said before; after that, the doctor should wash the head of the patient, then make a cauterization on the head and one on each horn, one behind and three at the back of the neck; and if you need to do more, and the body is moist and the patient suffers and is dying, make three cauterizations at the back of the spine; and let it be until the last cure is burned, and lift your hand; after that, the doctor should continue until he is healthy, and the cauterizations that are called "olive" as we have said before.
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsia
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The person with epilepsy should only use the fire cautery if they are feverish; first, wash the head and then perform other treatments that we have mentioned in the section on treatment when the patient is ill and suffering from fever.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	If it is a child who cannot tolerate having their head washed, make them gargle and chew by frequently washing the head with good meat; then, put the child in the middle, and apply the cautery according to what we have said before, and also cauterize the neck and each horn; and if the patient is out of sorts and suffering, apply the cautery as I said for one who has paralysis and stiffness of the body, on the spine of the back and the neck, and apply olive cautery according to the method I have described.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is a child: "Apply a fine cauterization according to this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When because of melancholy there are excess fluids or腐烂的潮湿，那么就用部分火烧法像我们之前说的那样治疗麻痹的人。
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	When because of melancholy there is excess fluid declining into melancholy, and the patient's body is moist, then he should drink something to clean his brain, according to what we have said about the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After removing the patient's hair; after making a good turban out of linen, also making it into a circle, if you put it on the head; and keeping the patient in a proper position, and well held together from all sides; then presenting the turban, and wetting it with old butter; and heating it gently over fire, so that he can bear it; after taking the turban off and letting it cool; and doing this to the patient every week once with another good treatment, until he is healthy.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	And so you see, if you cauterize it with fire, by making many punctures all over it.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This way of cauterizing the scalp evenly; and then put on cotton soaked in water and in grease from goat's milk.
de l’awe des eulz	of the hair
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When it comes first to the hair by the signs that I have said in the division, then begin and do the following: drink purifying thing for the scalp, and ward off all moisture, and make him sweat or bathe many times while fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	Afterwards let him wash his hair, and let him cauterize the scalp, and let him make two cauterizations on the two temples because it comes first to the hair; or if it comes first to one temple, then do it for both at the same time, and cut off all the hairs; and let him drink a purifying thing for the scalp, and ward off all moisture, and make him sweat or bathe many times while fasting. After that, command him to cauterize his hair, and let him make two cauterizations on the temples according to the width of the head; and beware of burning the scalp, and if you see too much hair burning, then stop it with water as you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and in the incision, how you shall put out the fire; neither is it good to put out fire by means of salt or damps.
dou cors des larmes	the heart of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	When the tears of the eyes are old and accustomed and are on the veins, or cut the arteries that are in appearance at the top of the head; and it is seen that it is of the cold and phlegmatic surpluses, then he makes the fire that I have said at the beginning of the awed descending to the eyes: I cauterize the top, and II cauterize on the II temples, and II cauterize where they pricked the II bones; and if it is necessary more, if he cauterizes well on the brow at all a small fire.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	the heart of tears within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you apply the medicine according to what we have said in the division, and it does not benefit, then do three nights of drinks for the sick person; after that, he takes up his head, and makes a fire cautery in the middle of the cautery with olive oil; and make two cauteries of the cautery called 'clavis' on the two sides, a little off the hair; and guard the artery so that you do not cover it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery called 'clavis':
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the paper of the oil is softened by disease and moisture, then the cautery of this cautery called 'olivaire'.
de coi ci est li forme:	of which I will tell you:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	and if you make two cauteries on the two sides as long as the hair is; and do not let go of the hand until the third part of the paper has burned, according to the way that I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	dou poil qui point l’oil
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	At times the hair of the oil is converted to the palatine, and pricks the oil, and there are made two kinds of cauterization: namely, by fire or by fiery medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they have grown and are equal, then put the patient to you; then sign on the paper of the eyes a figure which is also like the feathers of the mirror, and this is the beginning of the sign of the release of the hairs; then put cotton wet in wax and musk of pear on the oil, then heat the cauterizer so that this is its form:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After you have cauterized the wound little by little several times, so that the scar is burned at that place; and the sign of the health of the work is that you see the paper retreat, and the hairs stand up at the point where the oil is; then put your hand down, and leave it like that for III days, then put cotton wet in oil on it until the scorching is stopped; after the cure of the wound until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if after this the hair comes back, and the paper is softened, then start again with the cautery on the same level as before, as you did first; and if the hair has gone away, then cauterize until the paper returns to its natural state, and is even, and does not touch the hair the oil.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The medicinal fire cautery is that you command the patient to leave the hairs long and even, then make of parchment the shape of the bay leaf; then take French soap and very hot water, each a .Z., and grind them well together; and do it quickly, so that it does not cool down again, then in the shape you have made like the bay leaf, and put on the paper; and if the disease is only in one oil, so must one act in I, and also in both; and pour thereon the cotton wet in oil; and the patient's head be in your own health, and put your little finger showing towards the medicine, and press it a little and move it every time the patient feels tingling from the medicine, for he feels tingling too like fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	Once you have done this for a long time, take the medicine to your mouth.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the medication has passed, raise your head and look if the paper is raised as it would be if it were lifted by fire or by incision; and if so, then it is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If not, then again put more medicine on your head where the medication has not worked, as long as your hairs are even and combed; then put cotton wetted in balm on it until the itching has gone, after treating the spot of the ulcer that is called 'dyaphines' and others, until it is well.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you must keep your hair in place by means of many combs so that the medication does not get into your hairs.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if the paper becomes soft after, and the hairs are pricked by oil, then begin again the medicine on that very place that is softened by the paper properly, in the same way as you have done before; after treating until it is well; and this is the form of the fuel of myrrh:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the eyes of men are different in size and shape, and according to what you are constrained; and do not be answered with the right path for those who have the study of this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	The treatment of fistulas by cauterization:
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When treating fistulas as we have described in the division of diseases, if your treatments do not benefit, then it is appropriate that you perform cauterization according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to place his head in your lap; and with a damp cotton ball or persille juice on oil, heat the cauterizer, and bring it close to the hairline at the base of the scalp, keeping it steady; if you see, adjust the position of the cauterizer from one side of the head to the other, and if you don't see, keep it steady like a tent pole; but anyway, this that is heated should be applied for your treatment.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	Apres press the fistula will open itself, and treat the pus and dryness; and if it closes up, then operate upon it, and firmly hold the knife at the part next to the oil on your hand, so that your hands do not go wild; and place the knife in the fat of the oil, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the cauterization just at the bone, it would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, then start cauterizing again, and if you need to do it more, and let it rest for three days; after that put cotton wet in the burse on it, and cure the dry wound until it is healthy, and if forty days pass and it is not healthy, then apply corrosive water to the bone; and take care according to what has come to its chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And I have a way of treating fistulas which no one of the ancients spoke of.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Listen to me on how to treat fistulas, and don’t let it be open; then put in the small hole a fine needle so that this is the form:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and I pour in the quantity of an inch of liquid; and hold your hand firmly, so that the patient does not move at all, that the liquid does not run to his oil; and you must put on cotton wool dampened with water or vinegar over the fistula, the liquid if applied artfully will go into the place of the fistula, and heal him miraculously.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	If the fistula is healed by the fire treatment that we have spoken about, then it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, then you must cut into the nose, and bring the fistula to the edge of the nose according to what one should do in his own place.
des crevaices en levres	crevices in lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Mouth times have had crevices in the lips which are called "hair", and most often in the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these crevices as we have said in the division, and the cure does not benefit, then heat a small surgical knife according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it directly in the crevices until it is hot enough; then apply the cauterizer to the area until it is clean.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess comes in the root of the throat or in the larynx or at the roots of the teeth, after having caused pus and swelling and it has become a fistula; and you treat it as we have said in the divisions, and it does not benefit: then you must have fire according to the quantity of the fistula; after sealing or piercing the fistula, and keeping your hand until the iron comes out at its bottom, and doing so once or twice, after treating as we have said in the treatments, until it is healed; and if it is healed in this way, it is good; and if not, you must uncover the area and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in its [medical] book.
dou movement des dens	the movement of teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are soft from moisture and the teeth move, and you cure it with medicines, but that does not work, then put the chief of the sick in your mouth; after heat the cautery whose form will come later in a certain way so that you put a string on the tooth; and place the cautery hot inside, and hold your hand so that the sick feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth; after release your hand and continue the cautery according to your will; after fill the mouth of the sick with dirty water, and the scum a hour and clean thoroughly.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	In that way, the tooth that was moving is secured, and the gums that were soft are tightened, and the moisture that corrupts is dried up.
de la dolor des dens	of toothache
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When toothache comes from cold, or when there is coldness or numbness, and medicines do not help, then one should cauterize in two ways: and fire cautery and butter cautery.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Here is the translation of the text line by line: 
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	The fire cautery all at once if it is such that you squeeze a iron or brass ring, and thick so that the fire does not come to the mouth of the sick; after heat the cautery, wherefrom it will form itself thus, and put it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery has cooled; do this often, for the pain will be increased the day itself or the next day.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is necessary that the sick person fill his mouth with good butter in the application of this cautery, and then quickly remove it; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make a cautery of the root that you want, and according to what you have power; and this is the form of the ring:
des scrophules	of scrofula
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the scrofula is of cold moisture and is not obedient to digestion by medicines, then heat the cautery root with this being brought here afterwards, and it will form itself thus, and have II openings for the fumes to rise to the cautery from the other side; and put the cautery hot on the abscess once, or where it is necessary, as long as it comes to the bottom of the abscess; and if the abscess is small put cautery according to the quantity of the abscess, and let it be thus III days; and put cotton wet with oil onto it until the burning is over; after treat the wound with onions and tentings as long as it is healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	The shape of the cane:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When the moisture prevails over the throat, and most importantly when it comes from a cold complexion, then the patient should be voided first by solvents medicines; afterwards he must make a cautery on the root of the throat, and you must not come to the throat, and do not dare to stop but a little.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterwards he makes another cautery on the joint of the neck at the base of the spine, and this cautery which is called "clavicle", so that we have the shape in front of us; and cure the place as we have said before until it is healthy.
de la toust	of the toast
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite. de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.

et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and cauterize it until he pierces it as far as the cost of the heart, and comes to the figure of the cautery with four cauterizations; and for this one is made a cautery with three nails, so that the figure of the cauterization consists of four cauterizations; and the nerve is according to the subtility of a tent and this is the form of the cautery which has three nails:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And no time is applied on this nerve for there are eight cauterizations.

After putting on the fire cautery, rub it with salt; then let the patient rest, and do not move the limbs for a long time until they are well fixed.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated from above, what happens then? Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	Car li jointure est refermee, et estoste li moistor, et est sanez li malaides.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	For when in the stomach come coldness and moisture until it is removed from its color, and there are many catsarrows to it, and the manners of usual cures do not benefit it, then it is necessary that the patient be placed on his back, and his legs and hands be extended.

Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment for the wound that we had before, as long as he is healthy.

Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	And if your will is, then cauterize these cauterizes of the cuttle, if you are subtle and wise in the art, and guard yourself so that you do not burn all over, for you would make the whole body dry; and let it come to a spark, because the scar is very fine in place, and its wisdom to see.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When there is an abscess in the liver, and you can discern whether it is in the parenchyma of the liver or in the capsule: if it is in the parenchyma, the patient feels a slight pain; and if it is in the capsule, the pain is very intense.

Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cet cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.

dou cautere de pleuresin	double cautery of the pleurisy
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancient people said that one must do for the pleurisy double cautery of the roots of arista loga, and in a way: take one root of arista loga long, the most large that you can find, and is also dry, and is also as large and as long as your two hands; and moisten it with oil, and hold it to the fire, and cauterize I cauterize between the forceps and the chin, and II small cautery a little descending in the part who is desoz the beard; and II cautery between the fifth rib and the sixth, declining behind a little; and I cautery emmi the breast, and another on the stomach, and one between two shoulders, and two ribs after the breast cauterized who is between the shoulders; and do not press your hand, rather open it completely as when you are smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And no old man used fire cautery resembling a razor, and he rubbed it and put it between the ribs until it reached the abscess; and he jumped out of pain, as we have said in the incision of the liver.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work there is fear or the patient dies now, or a fistula comes from which cannot be cured.
de la mice	of the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin. de ydropisie	from dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Do not cauterize with a method called "asclytes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you have treated it according to the ways that we have spoken about in divisions, and your treatment does not help, then it is necessary for you to make three cauterizations around the boude (abdomen), one on the stomach, one on the liver, one behind the back on the spine, and one on the pis (pelvis); and let the cauterizations be very close to the joint of the limb.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After remove the fire cautery so that it goes long and slow, and do not stop the patient's cure after the cautery; and the healing would hurry, and both intentions will be together with the help of God.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The shape of the cautery for the belly is the claw that we have before mostrit; and this for the back is olive-shaped, according to what it is written here.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the joints
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner. Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too deeply, so as to burn the flesh, and be the cautery according to this form:
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After do on the legs two cauteries in each leg at the tip of the cuticle; and be the cautery long, one above the knee before and the other behind, between the legs; and leave the cauteries to rest for a long time without stopping, so that the flesh does not burn; after, cure with other cures that we have said.
de la menoison	of the mansion
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	When the solution from the stomach comes from cold and moisture, as long as the virtues that retain and digest in the stomach and in the intestines are affloiled, and cannot be cured by any kind of cure; and you see the patient very sick and of great virtue, then do a great fire cautery on the stomach according to what it has spoken of before or the fire cautery of the stomach, circulating; and IV cauteries around the navel carefully with all cautery nails, and II cauteries on the buttocks.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the moisture abundant and the patient suffering, then do a cautery on the hand, and I cautery on each finger, and II small cauteries on the stomach carefully, for the cure is profitable when there is good help.
de la cure des emorroydes	of the cure of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When the hemorrhoids are in the foundation, or one or more, and they are old and are large cold and moist humors corrupted, and they are cured as we said in the divisions, and it does not benefit if you do fire cauterization: III on the spine of the back, that is all far from sore little by little in triangulating, and I cauterize sore the two bones; and if you think that his stomach is cooled down, and the meat does not cook, and we see swelling the face, then let the face have a great cauterization on the stomach, as it is said before, and another on the liver, and another on the mouse to all cauterize nailed; and leave the cautery open for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After you have cured the fever as much as possible.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the flesh that is called "thelue
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you chop the arthritus, if you heat the cautery that seems like a razor, and then put it all burnt on the chopped arthritus; and let your hand so that the cautery comes to the birth of the vein, from which it is free; do this once or II, and if there is much arthritus, cauterize each one as we have said; after the cure of beneficial ointments until they are sane; and if you cauterize with a big cautery on the armpit, it will give more help.
de plaie mal curee	of a badly cured wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot bear cutting or opening, which we will tell you about in its place, comes a disease that cannot be cured except by cauterization.
