Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When there is a fistula that is raised and covered with pus and corrupt moisture, you must provide a delicate tent, and be sure that you know how much it has of perfection.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	After heating the cautery that seems like a razor, and pouring it into the fistula according to the quantity that entered it, and repeat the cauterization until the course of corruption is finished, once or twice, according to the quantity required; and be careful not to hurt the nerves that are there, and large veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	Once the fistula has reached the belly and intestine, take care of these places, and do not burn them except in the charned part, and be sure that it is not dangerous; then heal the place as long as it is healthy, and if the matter has been expelled, know that the place is whole again; and if the matter has not been expelled, know that the place is triply corroded and corrupted to the bone's bottom; and thus, as one of these that we will say in its place.
de la maladie des reins	of the disease of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When the pain of the kidneys comes with a heavy wind and does not take to women, then it is necessary that you make a cautery on the kidneys from both sides by the cautery that we have mentioned above; and if we make them in the middle, there will be three cauterizes in a line, and they will do greater good.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from pain and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then you make a cautery in the posterior portion above the bladder, where the hair of the pubic region comes together, and one on each side, making each cauterize as long as a penny; and you make one cauterize behind the back, where you need it; and you make the cauterizes clavate according to the form mentioned above.
de la marris	of the mare
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the marrow is cold and moist, and does not allow the conception of a child, and the flowers are corrupted and their time has passed; and when they come, so great is the pain: then it is necessary that three cauterizations be made around the buttocks, as we have said in the cauterization of the bladder, and two cauterizations behind the back; and let the cauterizations be clung to, as we have said.
de la hainche	of the hips
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous moisture descends into the hip joint box, and for this reason it moves away from its place, and the sign is that the thigh is farther away than the other when they are measured together; and the joints are found by touching them with the finger, then you must cauterize the patient on the hip joint box at the apparent circle, and mark before the joint around the box as it comes back, so that the box is within the circle; and if so, then the cauterizations are such as those which have been used to cauterize the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this fire cautery is not present, make three cauterizations with the olive oil, and let the cauterizations be complete as well; and heal until he is healthy.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain of the hip
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When the pain comes in the hip joint, and it is caused by cold and moisture, and the patient is cured of what we have said in the division, and the cure does not work, and the disease is old: then you must purging the patient of large humors with foul pills, or other bad-looking pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	After that, make the cautery; and the method of the cautery is as follows: namely, together with burning medicines, and fire cautery.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Fire cautery is according to many methods, some of which are as follows: first, make three triangular cauterizations in accordance with this shape, and make them deep and wide, and leave a space between each cauterization the size of two fingers, and let the olive oil cauterizations; never make a cauterization in the middle on top of the hip joint chief, for there are four according to this shape:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see that the fire cautery is at the circle that we have mentioned in front of you in the dislocation of the thigh; but do it in such a way that the circles contain all the thigh, and all the flesh of the knee is burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the way it is done in sciatica, when the pain persists in the thigh and does not reach the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if the pain extends to two or three inches above the ankle on the left side, and is felt as far as the toes or near them, then fire cautery should be done at that point, two or three times; either cutaneous cautery or burn the thickness of the flesh; and if the patient feels that the pain spreads to two or three inches below the ankle or near it, then fire cautery is done at that point, which is called "poins".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if he is a tailor, do more to him; and if he feels that the pain is going from the knee to the thigh, make a cauterization with a cutting cauterizer or circular one, and give him good guard in all your cauterizers so that you do not let go of them even as much as the cauterizer burns the nerves and large arteries, and do not cause more pain and contraction to the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I have also seen many who have made a cauterization on the heel of the foot, and left it so long that the leg was all swollen, and the toes as well, and was pierced and corrupted all the toes.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a solution of the belly which he had death.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pain is in two parts together, make cauterization in one and in the other, according to this way.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And the wise said in the cautery of the anus, for which this is the way, make it as big and thick as a thumb or less, and be between cleats and also from one cleat to another with space the quantity of a pea; and let the cleats project on both sides, and be also like knuckles, and I have much well-made iron; and this is the form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be heated until it is all red and wet, and then put it on the chest of the troubled anus, and turn it around the lower back; and cauterize once, and let it rest for three days; and then make a plaster with wax, and leave the open wound long; after the cure of poultices until it is well.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasis says that we use little of this cautery because of the fear of its poison, and few people use it; but it is a good cautery which can bear it, and where it afflicts.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The medicine cautery of fire is such that you make a tool with an edge on the margin of the door, and of either brass or iron to a long wall, and at a height there is II us, and II between each there is the quantity of the thickness of a thumb; and let them open out and up, and join together according to this form:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	After putting on the chest of the hip to the patient lying on his back, and quickly place your hand much above the chest; after that, pour in between the II circles of hot metal which is heated by fire a little, and leave it for an hour, and allow the pain and burning of the patient.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l'estrument et leve la hainche d'awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l'eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d'oignemens tant qu'il soit sanez.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	For the type of mortification that is like fire, and when it has passed, place your hand with the instrument and lift the foot with soft water, and leave it for three days, and put cream on it until the black blisters form; and let it be for pus in the blisters; and he who is behind should help after the treatment with onions until he is well.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take alkali and live charcoal, as much of one as of the other, and grind them together, and put them in a nine-pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	Take some fine sand from somewhere that the tip of one stick can pass through; and place that pot on top of another well-lined pot, and place alkali and charcoal and some sweet water inside, so much as to cover the two powders when you shake them well with your hand; and leave it like that until it has dried up a little water and has cracked, then take all that water, and pour it over the charcoal and alkali as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And if it has become very dry and is reduced to mud through the work of medicine and other cauterizations, for it does such a work as fire, and with other medicines which are well mixed together with soap, all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And the Gallians tell us of a cure wherein an honorable man was cured of the pain in the hip and sciatic vein; and he had much trouble, and they said that no other cure was done, and that he was healed with one soul when this cure was made, and he bathed himself as it is taught hereafter.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And he said in this way that you grind the green and dry lead, and mix it with a little fat, and put it on the hip and the thigh and the leg where the pain is, and let it be; and leave it for III hours, and in as much quantity that the patient does not feel the burning anymore.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then let him enter or bathe as long as his body is a little warm, and he lets the water in, and the pain will go away all and be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one must use fire cautery of such medicines, unless after the evacuation of blood.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Діascăřides saith that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with the ends of a goat's horn, then it heals much; and this cauterization should be done in this way.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take another and rub it with strong oil, and put it on the pit that is between the thumb of the hand and the other which is called the little finger.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	Afterwards take dry ends of a goat's horn, and hold it over fire until it is red-hot, and put it on the wool, and leave it there until it is blackened; and do this again, and do not cease to do this as long as you think that it comes up to the hip, and that the pain has stopped; and this way of cauterizing is called "cauterization with a goat's horn".
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain in the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, or by rubbing or by too much evacuation, or by the appearance of cold expanded matter, none of these appearances is worth remedies except for that which comes from an infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is appropriate that after the patient has voided any foul pills or other things, a poultice be applied to his back where the pain is, three signs of the cross in each line, and as many cauterizations as the patient can tolerate in each line, using the cautery called "poins"; and if you see, do III or IV cauterizations with the clavicle cautery according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This disease often comes about in small children, and the signs of the beginning are that they have a narrow stance when they stand up, and fear; and you will find behind the spine of the back and on us the appearance that comes upon the others.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you see it heal, if you cauterize it with fire according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So that the fire cautery is applied equally to each part of the spine.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see, then cauterize within the spine with fire that is two or three lines long, and let the pokes be close to each other.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	Afterwards heal the area as much as it is healthy according to what we have said, and beware that you do not apply fire in gibbosity which is in the spine of the nerves.
de la dolor des jointes	of the joints' pain
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When joint pain comes out due to moisture that spreads to each member of the body, and when the pain comes in pieces, what is called properly 'podagra', and when it is of a cold cause and cures of medicines cannot heal it, then it is healed by fire cautery in this way: Make the fire cautery within the joint of the foot, and let the fire cautery be olive according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if I need you to hold on the face of the foot, he makes a fire cautery with all the fire cautery that is claimed "no".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come up to the genitals and other joints, and this happens many times, he makes a fire cautery on each knee III cauterizes or IV of each part, all olive cauterize; and if you need more, you do more, but do not hold your hand firm except as long as the skin of the cure is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend to the genitals and back, he administers the cauterize that we have spoken in his chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, he makes a point of the fuse II lines; and if there is still pain in the two, he makes a point on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come up to the neck or shoulders, he cauterizes each part, and does good governance to the patient and applies medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you do this with good governance and you flush out the phlegm, then you will be healthy with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	regarding the rupture of the syrup
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When the rupture comes in anger, and the bile descends down to the bowels and is newly formed, then it is necessary that when you look at him, he does not vomit that day; and he uses things that leave his belly empty, so that the end goes down from his belly; after that, let him sit on his back between your hands, and order him to shave his beard as long as his bile is repaired, and bring it to your two hands, and sign with a stick above his spine at the knuckle, and in all places that are similar to half of a circle above his chest; then heat the fire of which this form is:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	as long as it is white and lets out drops.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then put the balls back in place; and the minister should dip his hand so that it does not turn back; and well work on the legs of the patient, and put a cup to him I cussin and I serjant on the legs, and one other on the toes that he dips his hands; then put the fire cautery on his mark on all your hand, and hold it tight and hold it as you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, come again another time until you come to the bone; and be careful that the ball does not slide when you work on the cautery; that you do not burn it; and that by this the patient does not die, or some other misfortune.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you come to the bone with the fire cautery, your work is worth nothing.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is necessary that the fire cautery of children be fine according to their measure, and of great people also great according to their measure; after three days cure the place of the cautery with butter until the heat is gone; after it cure other remedies until it is well, and let the patient lie on his back for 40 days until the wound is well fixed; and it is necessary that his bandages be kept in place for a long time, so that the ball does not slide when he goes to bed.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after 40 days, when he wants to get up, a well-made girdle is brought to him and worn for 40 more days; and let him have good rest, that he work little and guard against too much drinking and eating, and against too high heating of the body; and when he has done this teaching, then is he entirely sane.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say here after the cure of surgery in his medicine.
de la routure dou ventre	from the rupture of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures come in other bellies and are known, and you see that they no longer grow, then he does I the cautery of the cautery according to its quantity, and let it be burned with fire the third time of the cure; after the cure according to what we have said; and no one of the old has said that one should cauterize at the cautery at III angles according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but the first sign is to take an axe and make a line across the length of the cut, and another behind it, and all your hand holding the entire clamped cauldron.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first treatment is lighter and milder.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in any member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes in any member, or from falling or being hit, and this pain persists for a long time, and the medical cure does not help, then it is appropriate that he be cauterized with the cauterizer which is called "point," and the cauterization is done according to the length of the member and its smallness and its weakness and its virtue and its location from twists and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If he is well after the first cauterization, it is good; if not, start again on another part, for custom tells us that it should go to the member that is nearest to him, so you must do the cauterizations until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	of surgery
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	Surgery should be performed by fire cautery at any time, and most often by the patient suffering from the putrefaction of pus and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	You should be careful that the disease is just beginning, and if it has already begun as described in the division of maladies, and does not improve or remains stationary, and you are unsure whether corruption will spread throughout the entire body, then perform V cauterizations on the head: I cut off the hair at the top of the head, and the other toward the forehead near the hair; and III on the II horns, and II behind on the nape; and let it burn so long with the cauterizer that it reaches the bone, and as long as the scabs come off without causing any vapor of bad odors to escape; and then cauterize the mole according to what is before you.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules; et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	Et s'il est mélangé partout, il perd manifestement; alors, si cela convient, tu le cautérises avec ces cautères que nous avons décrits au-dessus, un cautère sur la nuque, deux sur la colonne vertébrale, six sur le dos, un grand sur la tête et un autre délicat, deux sur les épaules, deux sur les côtelettes, un sur chaque articulation des mains et des pieds, et sur les creux des mains. Et tu te méfieras des nerfs qui sont derrière, afin de ne pas les brûler; et tu ne feras jamais de cautère sur l'os du poignet, ou sur celui de l'estomac, ou sur le foie.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And if it is mixed everywhere, it loses manifestly; then, if it is appropriate, you will apply the following treatments described above: one blister on the back of the neck, two on the spine, six on the back, one large one on the head, and one delicate one; two on the shoulders, two on the ribs, one on each joint of the hands and feet, and one in the creases of the hands. And you must beware of the nerves behind so as not to burn them; and you will never apply a blister to the wrist bone, or to the stomach bone, or to the liver. And know that when you make more blisters, you provide more help and benefit; and know that the patient does not feel pain from the blister as much as the healthy person feels it because his body is already corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cauterizations are great and small according to the members and joints, according to what you will find in the manner of iron.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After healing, let the bread of the flour be with honey and other cures until it is healthy.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the swelling comes to any member and is healed with medicines, oils, and poultices, and it is not healthy, then let the cauterization be made on the member according to its size and greatness; and may the cauterization enter a little into the flesh of the cure; and then heal with ointments until it is healthy.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And no time is made to cauterize and by hand and by foot and by back, at the exit of the nerve that moves the member, and thus if it is injured; and yet there is no problem if one does not know the members and the exits of the moving nerves of the body.
de albaras	of barbers
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the "albaras" patient is awake and the medicine does not help, then cauterize with a fire cautery a little perfectly, according to the quantity of the juice of curcuma, until the blotch is opened and its color changes; then cure with flour of dates and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood of crow and blood of pigeon, each of them in part; and mix them all together, and bind them with a cloth, and apply it to the affected area until he is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	the cure for leprosy by cauterization
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When the leprosy appears at the beginning, and you see it stop, if you cauterize with a fire cautery that seems like a circle, all around the edge of the leprosy.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And yet many say that you should also cauterize in the middle of the leprosy; and yet I do not think this is good, because I fear it will become ulcerated and腐した、そして私は一度もそれを試したことがない;そして、私が聞いた最も正しいことは、それが周囲の火傷の周りに cauterizedである、
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When someone has a disease called "adubelati", and it takes long to die or because of the waste it creates or because the sick person is too old and has little blood, or because they are very weak; then you see them hasten to die: so cauterize them with small fire in piercing; then leave them like this.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For they will hurry to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you pierce them with all the cauterizing, then heat the cauterizer so that it is hot:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And put your hand in the middle of that disease called "adubelati" as long as the cauterizer has pierced the pus, and let it be such a cauterizer that the sick person feels the cold in some way so that the course of the pus is shortened.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the treatment as long as he is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	With fire treatment
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another way of sickness, which is called "corrodens," and is nothing but a putrefaction of the member, for it corrode the members as much as fire dries them up.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in its early stages that can be treated with fire, then heat the clavers small and large, according to what is suitable for the place where the illness is; after having cauterized all sides until you have completely removed all corruption, and nothing remains of it, so that everything that is corrupted is bone.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then leave it for three days, and put on the burned members oil until the burns from the fire are healed, and all corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the treatment with ointments that produce heat.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if you see after three days that the hair does not grow, it is good; and if not, then start the cauterization on that which has been delayed from its place corrupted.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this ointment has never yet been cured of medical fever in place of fire cauterization; but fire cauterization is of greater help, and I have already said that the cure of medical fever is in the division: take it when you need it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of onions that come from the field
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	For sometimes after the rains a disease that is called "close" according to our intention, and it is a great thing grown up that bleeds the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cauterization of this disease is in two ways.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	That is to say fire cauterization, and cauterization with hot water.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Cautery with fire if you heat the cautery like a pen of a vouteul, and let it be made of good iron to the measure that it can hold the nail from all sides, and that it has fine margins; after place all hot on the nail, and turn your hand completely around the nail until it comes to the head of the nail; and let it stay so for III days as soon as it begins to move putridity; then make a plaster of wild marjoram crushed with oil, and let the plaster on all night, and let the nails come out and will be rooted from their roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal the wound by applying charcoal until it is healthy.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if the neck is converted by defuers, and many times comes out and in hands and cuts, then it is necessary that you bring a cautery of hot water; and this is a way: take a chain of air or iron, or a pen of vouteul, and put on the nail and the althelul, that is to say porrels warts; and put the chain on it so that it turns red all around, then put a little hot water on it, and keep your hand well, and press your hand turning it so that the margin of the chain comes to the root of the nail, and can find the hot water way deep until the root; and let the patient feel a little of the sting of the hot water for an hour; then leave it, and it will be rooted from all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Make another one after this, as long as you have burned all those who are in the core, then treat the wounds that cause pain.
li cure dou trembler	He treats the shaking.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee; et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some shake from cold or the quarter-fever or other, so that you make them 4 or 5 cauterization on the spine of the back, 1 cauterization between each spine; and 1 cauterization at the feet, and 1 over the stomach with olive-colored cauterization; this will stop the shaking, and speed up the healing of the cold disease.
des pustules puans	of pus-filled blisters
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	No medicine appears on the body's surface, or pus-filled blisters, that come from corruzione materiæ grossæ.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	If the first appears that you make a cauterization on each head of the blister: a thin cauterization from a branch of mirth, which is taken up by the fire, or from a root of artemisia farida, or with a lente-shaped cauterizer.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And once the fire cauterizes him at the beginning according to this method, and he cannot grow hair in advance, but the excess is interrupted and he is healed; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut off
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	しばしば、切断された動脈から血が脈打つ音が聞こえ、それが傷口や潰瘍、火傷などの場所に届きます。これは非常に不快なことです。
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	そして、もし誰かが動脈を切り取られた場合（それは傷口や潰瘍、火傷などの場所に届く）、非常に不快なことですが、すぐに自分の人差し指をその血管の近くに置き、血管が収縮するのを感じながら、指から滴る血を吸い取ります。その後、オリーブ油で小さな火傷跡を治すために、小さなものでも大きなものでも、赤く焼いた石鹸を数回火にかけます。それから、傷やその場所に応じて、火傷の大きさに応じて、火にかけます。そして、その火傷の近くまたはその部分に、あなたの指先を置き、血管が収縮している間、火傷に触れないように注意しながら、石鹸を火傷に数秒間当てます。
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it jumps when you feel your pulse on the vein, and the cautery is warm, if you take another of the cauteries that are in the fire quickly.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not stop doing one after the other as long as the blood is stopped; and beware that you do not burn the nerve that is delicate, and that another evil does not come upon the patient; and know that when the artery is cut short of the blood vessel, it cannot be stopped well anyway unless by one of the four ways we have said: or with cautery, or with extraction if it has not been treated, or with a strong thread, or with medicines put on it which have the power to stop the blood; and bind and stretch it well.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will administer a strict binding with cloth or place burning things on it, or similar things, if it does not benefit, then do not.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	Et si ça arrive à personne et qu'il n'ait pas de mirre ni de remède présent, alors on doit mettre son index sur la plaie de la veine comme nous l'avons dit, et bien étirer jusqu'à ce qu'il soit réchauffé au-dessus de la plaie et de la veine; et ne bouger que le moindre, mais le mouiller avec de l'eau froide souvent car il faut que l'eau froide soit gelée et épaisse et réchauffée; et faire des incisions en avant de celui dont il a besoin de cautères et de médicaments.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of surgical remedies
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	Now we have told you in the first chapter all sicknesses due to fire, or burning medicine, and the wounds and causes and instruments and shapes of cauterization; and I put this chapter from the middle eye up to the top, and I will go in this chapter by that same middle path for those who are wounded more easily than those who are hurt.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so, since I am beginning to speak, it is necessary that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first chapter of the cauterization, and therefore it requires greater caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you that you do not take any foolish risks.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For in the manner of certain people come to cure.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	If they come from those who have so caused themselves that they die easily because of the mischief that they bring upon themselves by their illness and the greatness of their illness, then one should be afraid of them.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And of these I have who give you their sense, and say: "Wait, I am ready"; and the disease is contemptible.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It is not appropriate that you consent to these who come to you who have this manner, but put more great trust in your honor than in your covetise, and do not open it foolishly but carefully from him whom you are certain, and from whom you could have taken and lost; and use prophecy and indication in the treatment of your diseases so that health is converted; and whoever helps to acquire good reputation, glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, Our Lord give you good understanding and righteousness, and if you want to aspire to the holy inspiration of His hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I have ordered this chapter in speaking of chapters, according to that which is before or of the fire cautery, that I have devised for you from the beginning until the end, so that you may find it more easily than that of which you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	dou chief plein d’aigue
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Dou chief plein d’aigue: The head filled with water
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease affect adults except for children, and most of those who have it die; and from what I can tell, it is better to ease the pain with treatment.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child whose shoulder was swollen with water, and the head grew heavy every day until it couldn't be held up; and because of the moisture, he thought he was going to die, and this moisture came together so that it entered between the bone and the skin, between the armpit and the bone; and the ovraige is so great that the moisture enters between the bone and the skin, and the abscess is small, that you cut a large opening in the head; and also far away as we have seen, until the moisture runs; and see this form of the spitball:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is deeper, and the abscess larger, then make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	If the moisture has broken the bone and you see the joints of the skull open on each side, and the fluid jumps out when you press it with your hand, and it does not close again: then you should make three incisions in the shape of a cross on the skull:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, extract the moisture completely.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After removing the bandages and powders, put wine and oil on it, and leave it for five days; then remove it, and cure the wound with poultices and ointments, and allow the head to heal equally, and feed the patient dry meat made from moisture until the limb is comfortable and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is that you observe or opening the great part of the abscess, and the assembly of the sharp one; for it is not before; nor behind; nor on the right; and neither on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Cut then the place where the abscess opens, and the filling of the sharp one, and go according to what you can do; and guard so that you don't cover the artery; and come flur of blood, so that the patient dies from pain and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	in conclusion
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When there is a disease called "cataract" in the eye or nose, and the disease is old, and the cure of medicine does not help, then the last cure is that of cauterization with that which will cover the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It is necessary, therefore, when you have covered the eyes, that the patient should raise his chin; after he rubs the place with a rough cloth until the arteries appear, then extract the patient's hair from all of it; then look where the vein runs, and the roots of one and another are after the ears, and they are raised; then sign the roots, then cover them on both sides with an aggressive string made of two pieces, until the cutting comes up to the bone, and this is done by the thick part of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you see, close the spatium off the artery and the cap over it, carving also as I must on the traverse.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	When the vein is capped, let it continue to flow upward continuously.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open to the touch, then measure the quantity of the space of III inches, then sign off and cut to the bone; and what needs to be put out there is VI c/, and perhaps a little more or less, according to how the patient can tolerate it, and the refilling of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains on the bone no wound, then strain the wound and bind it, and the cure of ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	of grinding
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When the ancient catarrh comes, and for the moisture of tears and heat in the temples and ancient dry diseases and similar things, and it is medicated by the methods of medical treatment and all that does not benefit him, then we extract the arteries from the temples and cauterize them, as we have told.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the way to extract them is that the patient scratches his hair from his temples, and hears the artery opening in the temple, for it opens well with its tapping, and is little closed except in some men who are too cold; and if it is closed, then the patient's neck is stripped of some cloth, then he rubs the place with no rough cloth, and raises the place with warm water until the artery appears clearly; then take the spatula where this form is:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Then peel the skin lightly until you reach the artery, then turn it up as if pinching it, and remove the threads that are attached to each part; and if the artery is thin, then turn it with the tip of a hook, then cut it off from that part according to the quantity of II lines.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not cut, then neither does the sun shine on all things.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	If it is not cut, then neither does the sun shine on all things. And let there be a large artery, so that you tie it in two strong threads of silk, so that decay does not come before the time of the wound's outbreak, and decay comes from the blood; then cut off the surplus between the two threads at that same hour, and then, if you see, then cauterize with cautery cut to the bone as long as the head is cut; and this is the oevre of the muedre, if the patient does not have a fever and has a warm complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cautery is an aid to end moisture; for what is more powerful than that aid for moisture?
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Or let there be a cotton plug placed in the artery to stop the flow of blood; and when you remove it, then treat with dry medicines that make charcoal, and with tents, as long as he is healthy; and if there is no aid for the artery, so that you have to cut off by cauterizing, or you employ the place of vitriol and strain it with your hand so that the blood is stopped; and if you do not have any present, so put your finger on the place as long as the blood is frozen, and raise the place of cold water as long as the blood stops, and is drawn out as it should be; and the muedre and lighter in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein with a sharp knife from both sides, but let the knife be well sharp so that it can bear longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too soft, then it holds less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus; et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it must have between the two tools a space of an inch, and then when you have cut across the two ends, and you put on hot iron as long as it comes to the bone, and bend the vein in two ends; and are distant between the two shoulders because it is not souded from this cautery all through; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes flow down from the veins that are above the base of the skull, and this hot liquid does not benefit from any medicine that is applied to it, and you see the face of the sick person turn gray, and feel or movement so as if he were cold; and if the hair of the papilla is weak and moist so that the hair falls out, and the papilla is burned, and scarred by the heat of the tears, then there is a need for this cure.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they called the ancient "cure for contusions", and that is what you do to the patient who has this disease on his hair or forehead; then make three cuts equally along the length of the forehead; and let one of the cuts be like two fingers all the way down to the nose, and the others like two ribs above the cheeks, and keep away from cutting the arteries that are above the cheeks; and remove your hand from between the two jaws, and let each wound be as much as three fingers wide; and arrange a piece of sponge and a lot of cloth for him to suck up the blood, then pour the sputum out of both sides where this form is:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the incision that is to be made on the temple up to the second incision; and peel off all the hair that is between the two cuts down to the bone, then do the same from the middle of the first cut up to the other second one, and then remove this sputum:
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If one drinks in the first cut the instrument that is called "culteller", and is very well sharpened on one side, and on the other side it is blunt, not sharpened, and this is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the cutting edge toward the back at the end, and the edge is blunt toward the bone, and drink it so that in the middle cut.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And tie all the vessels that descend from the top at the end as the incision is continuous until it reaches the center, and then the other part does the same in the middle cut; and then remove the hair evenly, and express the blood; then put into each cut a cloth of old linen, and put on drapes wet with wine and oil and honey, and keep that the abscesses do not come; and on the third day unbind it, and there is much water, then wash it with cold water, and there is salt; then dry it, and put ointment of basil with oil of roses, and other cures for wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	let the hairs
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When there is a catarrh in the head by custom, and you see that the hairs are tense and small, and blur the sight, and the papers burn; and the hair falls out, and where it chief hurts there is pain that comes suddenly; then know from these accidents that those matters and that catarrh do not come but from many veins, and the cure that it brings is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And you command the patient to rub his forehead well, then make a wide cut across the forehead, and another that is large under it.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And you begin the cut on the left temple to the right temple, and make an incision up to the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves that move when one cries; and when the bone is exposed, then dip all the blood in a sponge, and then cover between the II lips of the cut with cotton wicks, and moisten them with vinegar and oil, and be careful not to burn the aposteme; when it has been extracted, then you should rub the bone until it begins to grow, then cure it with drying things, which cause chills.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take II parts of flower of wheat, and III parts of colophony, and make an ointment; and administer it to these wounds to stop the spread of gangrene.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	the aching in the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that causes an aching in the ears is one of the IV things: grain, beast, stone or similar thing like iron; seed, like seeds, peas; fluid-like thing like water and easily moving and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it aching in the ear is a stone or another thing that does not fit into the ear, and does not get stuck in the ear, then put the ear to the sun.

Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Mouth times comes through with this treatment; and if it does not come through, the patient is given extraction with fine tweezers, from which this form is derived:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes through with tweezers, it is good; if not, the patient is given extraction with a fine scalpel of small double-edged blade; and if it does not come through by this means, then take a piece of air from near the ear lobe very firmly, and stop what is inside the ear with soft wax so that the sound cannot enter with the air; then the treatment should be successful, because many times comes through as we have said; and if it does not come through in some way, then hold the glans in the hand, and place a tool on it which is suitable for this purpose, and put a little cotton around it; then press the glans against a stone or something, and treat.

And if she does not come to all these things that we have said, then you hurry to split the ear as well as the abscess and spasms; and the way of the split so that you do first to heal the patient of the cerebral, and draw blood according to the measure of his virtue, then put the patient between your hands and turn the ear up, and make a small split in the root of the ear to fat where it depends; and let the split be also as a moon, until you come to the stone, then split the bone according to your power, and suck it gently into your mouth; and the cure until he is healed.

et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and incise that seed.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not make this while you think that the grain is moist due to the moisture of the ear, until you have made many attempts; then extract it with gentle pincers and on the suckers, as we have said, so that the extractions are controlled.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	So that with the ear the patient should use a sneezing of the first condition, and broadly wrap the ear with old cotton.
