s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	if she sits well like this, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	if she does not sit well like this, take many times the seed according to its length and slight movements, and heat it slightly by the fire; and put into the patient a little piece of her ear, and press upon it from the other side, and make a hole in the stone which is in the ear; and do not cease to make that hole with the seed until all the drip has gone, and then let her sit all right; and if you see this, take a bit of seed, and dip one of the seeds into the fire, and the other head take from the fire as long as that seed burns; then remake the other holes with other seeds until all the drip has gone, as we have said in the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of an animal's tooth, if it is small, as a flea or similar, treat it as we have described in the division; but if it is a large tooth, extract it with tweezers, and this is the lightest thing to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of earworms, when you treat them as we have described in the division and in the treatment of distillation, and the cure does not help, then you should look at the ear in the light of the sun: if there are no worms, extract them with fine tweezers, and if there are none, take hold of the hair by which it is attached.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	It should be narrow below and wide above.

And if there is silver or gold, they are drenched in the small holes, and above them to distil; and to press into the distilling in the instrument of brass, which you will see well, and if you have a razor and wrap the cotton tip forward; then pour your oil or juice, and what you will see of your medicines in the tube, and the tube is in the ear; then pour into the razor all the cotton, and press your hand with timidity until the oil is distilled or flowing from the ear; and let the patient smell it inside, and let the distillations be a little heated on the fire as they are distilled in the ear; and guard that they should not be too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the support of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without any perforations in their ears; and this same thing happens to men by the support of a wound, or a splinter inside the ear, and such supports sometimes completely come out of the ear, if one cannot see them; and they never cause any harm, and one can see well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	This, then, which comes out completely if one cannot see it, is of great damage in many conditions, and in this one can see that you should place the ear of the sick in the sun; and look inside: if you see the operation apparent, if the work has completely done all this hair of which there is this form:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And be smooth and thin in front and behind all over, so that it does not hurt the ear; if the operation is a splinter or a hook inside the ear, if one holds it closely, and the handle lightly, until this splinter is completely out.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the ulcer is fully formed in the ear, then take a fine, light razor and heat it slightly; then put it where the cork of the ear is.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	And if you feel the ulcer that the patient feels pain in the ear, pierce it lightly and be careful not to harm the nerves of the ear; then put a tent in the ear according to its width, and wet it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Make no attempt until the wound is healed, or take a tent and wet it with rosewater, and powder it with vitriolic broomiate; and if you see that the ear runs, let it be so that you remove the tent and move another tent wet with beeswax, which has been made with rosewater and wax, until the discharge is dried up; then treat it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if the pain comes, dip a sponge and cloth in cold water and put it on the ear, and use other remedies that stop the pain which are to treat the distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the paper
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	Take the root of a plant and let it dry out, then place it on top of a vitriol (a type of mineral) with tweezers or pins, so that it is exposed to the vitriol's vapors.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if they are not peeled, then cauterize them with a small, sharp cauldron, and let the cautery rest after the incision has been made; and often peel them, so that nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and never come back.
de la gresle	of the grayish-green substance
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Maitres fois viennent en papier des eaux une choses que semblent gresles en sa forme et en sa durece, et par ceu est ceste maladie apelee "grandine", et est une assemblee de moisteur grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est tels: pren garde se li grandine se mute d'une part et d'autre, et c'est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donc dou large, puis l'escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Many times come in papers of waters an things that seem gralesque in its form and in its durece, and for this the disease is called "grandine", and is an assembly of moisture thick in the paper above and under; the ovraiges are such: take care if the grandine mutates from one side to another, and it is a light thing to know; cut then broadly, then scorch each part lightly, then take it with tweezers, and wrap it up. If you cannot cover it without piercing the paper, do not harm the patient; and if the fracture is large, so the assembly has a seam, and cure as long as it is healthy; and if it is small, do not use force, for the ovraiges restore it soon enough and leave scars.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the aching is descending from the ear towards the part above, then turn the paper over, and let the ache be at a pinch, and the cop and press on both sides; and if the paper is dislodged by the incision, that does not cause any harm; and when the ache has been copped, then pour on the salt water, and cure the place from which it comes as long as the patient is healthy.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the hairs
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	is an acne that is produced in the form of paper webs above, and this happens more often to young people than to others, and grieves their eyes, and they come down with catarrh in the mornings, and they cannot look at the light of the sun because their tears hurry to their eyes; and because they lie on their faces immediately, and sleep on them, and their webs are moistened by the sweat that increases and changes the appearance of the acne that is formed in the oil.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the shoulder to your side and feel the extension between them.

And the method of this treatment is that the patient places his head in your lap; and then take a linen cloth, and set up a tent in a circular shape according to the quantity of extension between each part, then put it on him; and press with your hands from one side to the other, so that the extension is gathered into the circle; then cut through the middle of the moisture with a sharp knife, making a slit no larger than the wound at the base of the vein; and cut the skin completely until you reach the extension; and in several positions the extension comes out of the slit, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	So take away all the cloth between your hands at the back, and turn your hand from one side to the other until it is well spread out; and be careful not to twist in the slit, so that you do not come to the fat, or you will tear it.

Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such men who grind seige and put on in order to corrupt that moisture which is delayed.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal him as long as he is healthy.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it comes to the apothema of the hot steam, if the healer with salves soothes as long as he is healthy.
des poilz des papieres	of the hairs of the papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai. de la porriture de l’oil	from the decay of oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease, called "aleacrati" or oil decay, comes about in the oil, there are two ways it can happen: one natural and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And comes from a wound, or surgery, or cauterization, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the method of treatment in this is that you split that suture, and free the lips from it, and put linen strips inside, and leave it until it is healed; and it is not right that you use in the treatment of it things that dry and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the disease will come back worse than before; but use of softening things, such as fenugreek; and water or alcohol infused with seeds of flax are cooked, and olive oil is melted and mixed into it, and a tent is wrapped around it, and treat it like that.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasures of your treatment are that you take care that it does not heal in a way that is not good; and the following treatments that we have said are not right to use in this disease, so that it does not come back in the same form as before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the cart that comes in oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease that is dislocation, which is really called "axacrati," and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large. dou soudement de la papiere	Et si la maladie vient de fendure ou de couture ou de cautère, il convient que tu fendes une fendu re plainne desoz les poils des papieres, et selonc ce qui est ci devant; puis déploie entre les deux lévres d'une tente, si com j'ai dit; et il faut faire l'ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres apareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malade aussi, selonc ceu qu'il i convient d'ovraige et d'estrumens em plusors dispositions.

de l’ungle de l’oil	of the nail of the oil
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil. de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	the flesh that grows on the apple

de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the oil
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	I will address the fistula only: when you treat it with fire cautery and medicine as I have described above, and it is not healed, then cut open the abscess, let out all the moisture that is there, as far as the bone;
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed, and you will see corruption and blackness, then remove all the instrument with which it was deformed; and it is called "spiky head", and let it be made smooth like a file, as it is in this form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And put on the bone's corrupted place, then turn it between your two hands, and press with your hand a little so that you can feel that corruption has been removed; and do this once, then return to applying drying medicine.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the loins are tight and the belly is round, and if the cors of the bowels is tight as well, remaining so for forty days, and if it does not become swollen or inflamed, no bad accident will happen to him, except that he must return the fistula to the hole from which it came, according to this method: you must discover the bone a second time with an iron awl, and with bitter medicines; when discovered thus, take hold of the iron nail at three angles, and make the hole narrow up to the top as much as you see here.
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	If the loins are tight and the belly is round, and if the cors of the bowels is tight as well, remaining so for forty days, and if it does not become swollen or inflamed, no bad accident will happen to him, except that he must return the fistula to the hole from which it came, according to this method: you must discover the bone a second time with an iron awl, and with bitter medicines; when discovered thus, take hold of the iron nail at three angles, and make the hole narrow up to the top as much as you see here. Then place the awl on the delicate part of the limb, and remove your hand from the oil pot, then turn it completely until it pierces the bone and the patient feels pain in his arm; and when the medicines dry up, if the char has hardened the loins, the material will go to the arm; this is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the issue of oil
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the hair is completely removed from the whole head, and there comes no difficulty in putting on a turban, nor any reduction, if you leave the patient; then treat him, then put vials over it, filled with oil made from acacia and aloe and incense and myrrh, and draw out the oil, and apply the plaster of oil to bandages and drapes; and the way to use the drapes is that you squeeze the drapes enough soft, and double each one in four, and then put it on top of another according to how much hair there is needed; then draw out the oil from above a hard bandage, and begin again with the vials to suck without hurting; then take off the vials and leave the oil drawn out day and night, and it will be relaxed again; then take off the bandage after the day and night, and if you see that the oil is coming back, it is good; if not, then begin again with the plaster and drapes and bandage and vials until he is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	the tearing of veiled cloth
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When the disruption comes in the veiled cloth, then open it up, and comes forth as paper so much like grain of resin, and can be seen; therefore, if you cover it up, the ovations are such that you push a needle into the root of the part just above, then push another needle where there is double thread from the part of the armier; and let it pierce, and leave the first needle according to the arrangement; then take the double thread and tie one part of the uve around, and tighten it well, then remove the needle and put wet oil on the other uve; and leave it until the thread rubs with the uve, then treat the oil with soothing things as long as the wound is healed; and never does the wound become restrained by the uve each part of a circle of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the hairs have a good appearance, then pierce them with a thin nail that comes out perfectly from the oil, and cut off the moist albus and pull out the hairs, and leave it for a while; then extract it until it is healthy.
de la bowe de l’oil	the oil
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease, which is called "alcunnati," is only a kind of oil that is mixed together, resembling water descending, and is not water; and the manner of its appearance in the ovary is such that you place the patient on a padded seat and upright, then take the head between your hands from both sides, and move it up as you see the oil rise towards the hairs; then let it fall, and do not cut off the light, and observe how the hair looks like water; and if it does not descend, know that it is water, and let the oil-like substance appear in the same way as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you place the patient between your hands, then take the thin spatula and apply it to the corneal membrane with the help of the continuous connection with the corneal membrane and the crown, until the bow rises; and when it is released, pour it into hot oily honey or water or fenugreek that has been boiled and honey, and cure from another cure as long as it is healthy.
des aigues de l’oil	of the oil
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have the appearance of needles in the incision, and what is appropriate to pierce; so that it is done according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is appropriate that you place the patient between your hands, away from sunlight, and press the oil firmly; then take the instrument called 'almagda' in your right hand if the eyes are on the left, or in your left hand if the eyes are on the right; and then bring the tip of the instrument gently to the edge of the corneal membrane in the small area next to the tear, then turn the instrument back again so that it enters the empty space; and the measurement of the path of 'almagda' should be at the perfect measure of the space from the plum pit to the end of the darkness; and this is the crown of oil. Then you will see the bone in the paper because of the clarity of the corneal membrane, and then place the instrument at the level of the astringent water, then express one path after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If he is seated now, then see the patient in front of him and the instrument in his oil.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting for a little while, and then he raises the second way with force with the instrument, and when it is firmly fixed and does not rise, gently extract the almagas by turning your hand back and forth; and then put a little gold in it, and take it away from that oil.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then place on the other hand the stopped oil or another moistened oil in oil rosin and abundance of wax, and bind with the healthy oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Now, and those who are of our kind, let us put on a common thread with abundance of wax.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almagas cannot enter the oil because of its hardness, for there are some men whose hairs are too coarse, then you must press the instrument that is called "alberit", from which this form comes:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And so now the connective tissue, and do not go too far with it, but make it small, then pour the liquid in, as we have said; and at the completion of the work prepare for the patient a bed coming, since he sleeps on his back in the dark place; and let him be free from all movement, and press light meats, and do not move his head neither to the right nor to the left, and let him be tied according to his disposition until three days; then take it out again in that same dark house, and test his sight, and make him see some things, and then put him back in the bonds until the seventh day; and it is not necessary that you do this at the time of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you prepare this, because he will go up quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	As the seventh day comes, you shall pour oil before the seventh day, and address it with that which soothes the throat; and when it is calmed down, then take off the veil and put it on his face, on the right side, to cover it for one day, and be in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then go out of the house a little by little, and turn to his side; and know that no doctors should meddle in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us from the Land of Israel who told us that in our country it is said that one sucks water, but nevertheless I have never seen this in our land, nor have I ever read about it in any books of the old ones; and perhaps this is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	These are the shapes of the elements of earth, for whoever does not know them will see them; and they are properly made of air.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the head of this middle part be at an angle of three angles behind.
de la char sor le neis	of the shoulder above the neck
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	None are born or born various shoulders, of which there are none that seem scorpions at the mouth of the foot; and if there are such, or he has an enchiaved shoulder from a fox's fur, and a good-colored shoulder.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In those shoulders that are souef and not enchiaved, it is appropriate that you make the patient sit between your hands toward the sun; and operate his nose, and put the oncins on those shoulders, and tighten them well; for if you hold this small sharp tool of one side, as long as you know that this shoulder is all bone.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	If there remains nothing that cannot be covered, if you open all the instruments of the subtle light, so that it does not stay anything; and if he comes up to you, or an abscess, so the scar, as it should; and if these are malignant abscesses, hurry and cauterize them, so that the scabs are stained and all the shoulders are boned, then cut or born easily and quickly or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the newborn is sick, and moisture comes up to the palate, know that he is healthy; and if the moisture pierces in such a way that there is no room for the instrument to come: then it is necessary that you put a piece of linen thread about as thick as a finger, and tie both hands together with a space between each string of about one inch or less; and place the baby's chin on the thread in his hand, and pull it by sniffing it until it comes out through his nose into the mouth; and many times do this to the child in school, and this is a light task for him who does it; then hold the head that comes out of the nose with one hand, and the other head that comes out of the mouth with the other hand, and pull them one after another while keeping them together like us who are tying the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Make sure that the new thread has corrupted the thread, then treat the wound, wash the blood, and moisten the wound with Egyptian ointment, and put it back in place as before; make sure for III days or more, until the ointments have corroded whatever is delayed from the thread; and then put a piece of plaster on the wound for some days until it is well, and if there is need to use dried medicines, do so; and this is the form of the instrument to purify the head, by which we distil oils and medicines into the ear:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	Make it of silver or gold, resembling an open lamp, like a tube, and conduct it so; and if you see, make a closed tube, and this instrument is flat for purging the head; and I always have at hand to the head so that it can be held when oil or any liquid is heated.
de la char sor le neis	of the horse's shoulder from the neck
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times in the neck of the horse a disease appears that is called "telul", and it grows and becomes very large, so much so that it can be seen with the eye; and for this it is necessary that you chop at the beginning, and all the bone, then put on fire the cauterizing medicine; and if you delay to chop it until it is very large, if he has hard color, of poor feeling: if not touch him with iron because it is an inflamed abscess, for when you chop it once, great evil comes to the sick person; and the abscess is touched by light touching, not by red color, and you see that he can be all chopped, if he vacates the sick and chop him without fear, and cure him with dry and restraining things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the baby is born, cut and cure.
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when a child's teething begins in one of these cartilage joints, it brings little profit, except for those few who benefit from it.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	When a child teeths in one of these joints, it is necessary to cut and cure it; if you see that the wound is fresh throughout all its length, and then join the two lips together with a stitch, and cure it until it is healed; and if the lips are torn on one side or the other, you must scrape all parts with salt and dragon's blood powder, and burn them with resin; put these powders on a piece of plaster of strength or another kind of plaster, then leave it to itch by itself; and then cure it with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The way to stitch up an injury is this: either with needles, as we have spoken of in the belly-stitching; or with thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	With a sharp knife, cut off the tips of the lips, which are like grain, smaller and larger; then cover them with cotton and bind them tightly; and then employ the acid of vitriol on them, as long as the wound is still open; and then wash it thus, and dry the place well until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the teeth
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times have the teeth been pulled out with tweezers, which the old people called "albulus"; if it is necessary that you hold them with tweezers, and cut off at the root, and let the blood run; then apply acid of vitriol or other drying and binding powders to the wound; and if this tooth comes back after the incision, and many times comes back, if it is pulled a second time, and cauterized: if it does not come back after the cauterization, and that are the forms of instruments to pull.
des sordens	of the order
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	of the teeth
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure the tooth from the pain that you delay drawing it as much as you can, because there is no excuse for not doing so; because this is a very high substance until we have no excuse to draw it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	And then when the sick person is hard to draw out, it is necessary that you are firm with the teeth of the hollowers.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Several times the pain of the sick person has ceased, and he thought that the tooth was good, and made the tooth pull with a good tooth; and nevertheless the pain does not cease because of this, until the illness is removed, for we have already tried to do this to these patients; and when you are certain about the tooth of the hollowers, it is necessary that you scrape the tooth between your teeth very well with a hard instrument, then let it move back and forth, a little at a time, until it is well pulled, then tighten the pliers. And let the head of the sick person be in your good lap, and hold him firmly so that he does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After pulling the tooth correctly without breaking it, and if it does not come out, then take one of these tools and put it in from each side gently, and move it so as to have done so at first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if his jaw is pierced and filled with meat, then you must stuff it with cotton where the hole is; and if he is held carefully with pliers so that he does not break when removed; and it is necessary to wash well around the gums in order to clean out the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And you must take care not to break it, and there remains a part of it, and returns to the patient by the mischief of the root with greater pain than before.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And you must take care not to do so as the ignorant surgeon does, who, through his haste and boldness, often breaks the jaw without any consideration for what we have described; but brings about many things by the quivering of that great disease for the roots from which they come, or by the jaw itself that they break, as we have often wanted; and when the jaw is drawn out, if you wash the place with wine or oil or wax; and if it bleeds, stop the flow of blood there, so that it often happens, I say, as soon as one stops the bleeding with vitriol.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments, so that they do not mute the first tenons, are long in length and large in width, so that they do not double up when you draw the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them be big limbs so that they do not bend when drawn, and let them be well made of iron, and let them have teeth for holding.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root moves when drawn, it is necessary that you put cotton wet with oil on the joint or two or three days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	as long as the joints are smooth, for then the pliers that are called "algefri" seem to bite; and let them be made inside like a file, and this is the shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots will not come out with all these pliers, it is necessary that you uncover the tooth completely around the root, and put the instrument that is called "althali", that is to say file, so this is the shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be big and strong so that it does not break, and the root jumps out through this, it is good; if not, if you help with all the tools, from which the shapes come afterwards:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps with this instrument that has two rays, from which this is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools that are in front in the rasa
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let this instrument be strong so that it does not break, and know that many tools of the dens are; and also other tools, which are not counted; and the master subtile tries out his own tool by himself according to what his works and the disease show him, for there are some diseases where the old teacher does not teach a tool for the variety of them; and if it does not break the chariot or the other bones, on which he will lie, if he seeks the tools that suit him, which I have told you, and helps with gestures, from which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let it be large and firmly holding the bone so that it does not escape but can hold and remove; and then return it to the medicine's place suitable for this, and if there is pus in the bone, and it is small, then reapply all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth do not seem to be in line with the natural shape of the jaw, and their form is ugly, especially in young women, it is necessary that you know whether the roots are coming out after the tooth, and they are not in their right place, and cannot be sewn or filed: then cut off; and if it is connected with the tooth, take this instrument whose shape is similar to a small beak, and which is made of iron obtained from a smelter:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the cap fits and fits tightly because of the hard tooth, and so that you do not move the others, and if it seems that it can be filed, then take a file of this shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and is also like the lime whereon one makes needles; and in lime the tooth pokes and pokes with his hands lightly every day so that it does not move until it has cut; then the plane at the end to all razor, and its edge is too sharp and bleeds the tongue, so that it is necessary to sharpen the sharpness until it is even, so that it bleeds the tongue or corrupts the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth moves away
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	when the tooth moves forward with percussion or chewing, and the patient cannot press upon anything he chews until he has urinated, and you have treated them with restringent medicines, and this does not help; then it is necessary to restrain it with a gold thread, because silver wire becomes green and rusts, but gold wire never moves; and let the thread be neither too thin nor too thick according to the quantity of space between the teeth; and if you notice any gaps, take the thread and double it over the healthy teeth on either side, then place the bridges between the teeth, if there are one or more, until you have carefully cleansed them up to a healthy tooth on the other side; then restart the covering up to the part where you started, and squeeze your hand gently and carefully so that it does not move at all; and let your ligature be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then cut the chaps of the thread to a pair of pliers, and assemble them, and put them between the sound tooth, and set it so that it does not break the tongue; and then leave it so tight as it can stay, and if it falls, or the thread rubs, hold it with another thread; if it stays and serves this way all its time, and this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the joint of the II sound teeth, and the II bad ones, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth looses, if one puts it back in its place, little by little, as we have said; and do not meddle in this anyone who is not wise and patient, and never makes the form of a tooth of an old cow, and puts it back in its place where it has fallen short, and holds it as we have said, and delays and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	of copper the ring of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	No times is the ring of the tongue that comes from nature, which must be thus: or by accident of a sore wound; and the ovraige is such that you open the mouth of the sick person, and have his head in your hand, and loosen the tongue; then copper the large nerve, until the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if it is hard or soft, and it is sudden from a sore wound, so you bite it with the hook and copper the large nerve; and keep that the cut does not become too perfect, for the artery that is nearby; and when you have done so, take off the water of rose and thus, or cold water, then put desoz the tongue a piece of linen; and the loosing li malaides every night, so that the leus cannot soder.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if the blood flow comes on, then put vinegar over it; and if he goes up again, then cauterize him with the lentiginous cautery, which is good for that; and then treat him with other treatments until he is well.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see a small spot of black or white or hard, then the patient should not feel it or touch it, for that is cancer; and if it declines towards blotchiness, and there is moisture, then pour oncene onto it, and make it with a fine spatula, and deliver it from one side to the other; and if he goes up again to your opening, then put vinegar over it until it is dried up, then return to your opening as long as you pour it all out; then raise his head and neck, and treat him with other treatments until he is well.
des apostemes de la gorge	of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	the abscesses of the throat called "godath", and they are properly called "amandres"; and when you cure them, as we have said in the division, if they do not heal, be careful: if it is an abscess that is hard and white, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	If it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron either for fear of causing blood loss; but let it be as long as it is quiet, and then you will take it away, or else it would burst by itself; and if it is a white color, and the root is thin, then you shall have ready the instrument to cover it over, but first see that the abscess is warm and calm.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then make the sick person sit in the sun, and their knees be straight, and they open their mouth and place their tonguet between their hands, and press all the instrument against it, so as this is the form; and be of silver or gold as fine as our knives:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	And then press the tongue to all this instrument, and you will see the abscess, take the sharp knife and stick it in amber, and carry it up higher than you can; and do not tie any strings with it, then cover the instrument, from which comes the form, which seems a great strength; and yet their heads are bent and one above another, and they are very sharp, and are made of iron where or elsewhere:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, take the cope with pliers, from which comes the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And be it cut on one side and not on the other; and when you have copped one of the ambers, kop the other according to the same manner, and after the incision gargarize the patient with hot water, and repeatedly gurgle, and if blood comes up, gargle with cooked pomegranate juice, or leaves of wild mint, and similar things, until the wound is healed; then treat it as long as he is well; and never let there be more than two ambers in the throat, that is, the two ambers that we have mentioned above.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess in her throat, which is to say a small abscess; and I had it very tightly closed so that the woman could not breathe through the passageway that was blocked, nor eat or drink, and she would have died if she had waited another day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so large that it had risen two rain-falls through the two openings from which it was draining.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	So I quickly ran and put one of the suckers on it, then took a deep breath, and poured out a good portion of water; then I put another sucker in the other opening from which it was draining, and squeezed its tongue; after that I filled the sore with water, and it let out only a little bit of blood; and so the passageway in her throat became unblocked, and she began to drink clear water and then wine, and did not stop cutting at the abscess for a long time; and the abscess broke out again, and filled the space that I had cleared out, until it was very large; then I bandaged it and cauterized it inside her throat: so it stopped growing; and I left those parts, and only God knows what happened to them after me.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the swelling goes down from the eye, and it is gone and far away, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is large and round, it is called "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is healed as we have said in the division, and the cure does not profit, and you see that the abscesses are calm and thin, then you should cut them; and if they are round and assembled and are not far away; and they are bloody or of a red color or black, then you should avoid the incision of it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger with the disease.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is necessary then, when you see it, according to the way that I have said, of its bleeds and lontness, that you make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press the language to the instrument which we have mentioned above; and then put the incision into the eye, and turn it around, and cut with II instruments that I have said in the incision of II mandrels.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And you must not cover more than the superfluity that is beyond the natural term; because if you do so much, it will harm the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we said in the incision of the two mandibles, and heal until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has doubt about covering, then you must use fire cautery on the painful part.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the way of the cautery is sharp water.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And let the patient put his head in your lap, and then press his tongue to the instrument that we have said or fire cautery, and confound it with sharp water so that it is not too thick or too clear; and by using the movement of this instrument, from which this form comes:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let a cap stand on his head where the medicine is put, as if it were a spoon, and place the instrument we have said or fire cautery on all the medicine on the uvula; and let the patient lie down on his side so that saliva and mucus flow from his mouth into the medicine, so that it does not go down the throat and hurt him; then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it onto the uvula for half an hour, until you see it turn black and the medicine taste good; and if you need to refresh the cautery, dip the cotton in the medicine and put it back on the uvula; then let it dry, and after three or four days rinse it out with cold water, and cure it with gargling until it is healthy.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than the incision, but only the cauterization. If it is cured by fumigation according to this method, take calamus and ysope and oreganum and rue and chamomile and avronne and other herbs, and put them all in a pot or some of them in I can, and put it there easily, and make it boil; and the pot is well glued with strong earth, and add an instrument to it according to this method:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it is of silver or gold, and let one of the shoulder-blades be in the mouth of the patient as long as the vapor rises through the canal, until the urinary bladder is dead; then start again often, until the urine dries up, and guard against doing this at the beginning of the appearance of the abscess, because many things happen there; and do not do this except at the decline of the abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, then take a dog and put a nail in the mouth of the sick person so that the mouth does not get too hot; for the nail does not let the harsh vapor hurt the mouth, and it is good treatment together with salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Several times it goes into the throat of a fish or nothing; so it is necessary that you take what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you can see the thing; and if what is not opened for you and is pushed back into the throat, it is necessary that you make the sick person vomit so that his food is cooked in his stomach; perhaps then the thing comes out by vomiting; or the sick person swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a lettuce root, or a dry bread mooch; and you tie the sponge to it, and then swallow it; and when it comes to the place, if it hurts, then draw hard; and if it does not come out by what we have said, then take an instrument of plunk according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And so the instrument is curved at the tip to allow it to enter the throat more easily, and the tip is raised higher; and be careful not to touch the epiglottis, that none of it comes off, or push the bone in; and move it so that the patient swallows the instrument, for this is where the movement occurs; if he swallows it, or pulls it out far enough all at once, until it is out.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the blood from the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	There is no medicine that helps the blood, as I said in the division, by way of remedy with medicines; and when it does not benefit, then look at the throat of the patient to the sun, so that you press the tongue to the instrument which I have told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see blood, or pull it out with small tweezers that are sharp.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this does not work, then take a dog's tooth, and put it in the throat of the patient, then pour or blow the tooth so that it burns, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient's plague is of water all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full glass of cold water, and wrap it around the patient's mouth, and let it fall into his throat, and move it with his hand often; and if soon after that the patient feels the water, then spit.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not spit as we have said, then suffocate the patient with sage, using the instrument that I spoke of in the дымation of the wound; do this many times, because it will not choke.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the way of the fumigation is that you squeeze the blood from the nose or it has black bloody nosebleed, and let the water drop into a container in the middle, and let the instrument come out; then pour your smoke, and let the patient put the top of the cane in his mouth, and close his mouth, so that the smoke does not come out, but comes to the blood; and the blood will now come out, and if it does not come out, then start the fumigation again many times; and make the patient thirsty, and drink salty things and ale, and do not drink water; and then let him be well by this management.
