Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if they prick between the bladder and the half of the penis; and reach up to the join of the cunt, and up to the root of the cow.

Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula reaches up to the bladder or up to the conduit of the urine, if the urine sauts, and cannot be calmed by medicine.

If it is pierced just up to the join of the loins, then let him try coming up to his place; if there is no twisting and no invention of pain around the hips, then let him know that he has already come back in his place, and there is no medicine or hasty remedy by feeling, and these persistent abscesses do not have a cure except for work, and the vain thoughts of the foolish people who meddle with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	If it is not persistent and is not old, there is hope of health by surgery, as I have experienced, and that is that the patient lies on his back between your hands on his back; then he raises his legs up to his hips, and his hips are bent towards his abdomen; then pour a bucket of rain, or a plunger if there is twisting, until you know where the attempt comes from.

des emorroydes	hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are of two types: they may be inside the fundament, like grains of resin, and small or large, and there is a little or a lot of blood, and they have the color of the flesh; and the cure for those that are inside the fundament is this: you must instruct the patient to strain himself until the foundations come out, and let him spit them out; if he does not spit them out because of his moisture, then hold them with your fingernail, and cut off their roots; and if they do not stay cut off because of their moisture, then take them with a bandage, or cotton, or a piece of cloth; and pull them out with your fingers, then cut them off, and powder them with hot powders that are for cauterizing; or you cauterize them as it is said in the treatment of cautery, for other cures until they are well; and if the foundations cannot come out, then cauterize the patient with a hot clister to wash what is inside the foundation, so that it can come out freely; when the patient is straining, and the roots have come out of the foundation, then the cure is light; and it is done by holding them with your fingernail or with pliers, and cutting them off, then curing them as we have said, until they are well, and avoiding incision with iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary that you prepare the stitch according to this method: take a twisting thread, and put it in a needle, then pass the thread over the top and pierce the needle from the other side, and bring back the two ends of the thread through the needle, and if they are wide apart; twist the thread into a form, then tie it, remove the needle, and do the same with all the others, and leave it to draw out the excess blood; then put on the foundation a wet towel soaked in oil or balm, and put it on the foundation, and command the patient to rest; and then leave him until he starts to bleed, and when he stops bleeding, treat with ointment and other treatment until he is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	at the end of the stitch or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Often there is drying out at the end of the intestine due to its nature, and when the disease is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary that you cut off the skin from a spatumile or your nail, which does not leave it moist; then heal it until it is hard as it should be; and if it cannot be healed, then restart the rasuring more strongly than before, until it heals out, and is scarred; then heal it until it is healthy.
dou fremit	Do you fain?
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Is it painful? The formice is a small appearance of heat before the body, and it passes entirely; and there is no pain in it, and one can also feel it as though one were dead, and it spreads throughout the whole body, and more in the hands than anywhere else.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the healer should take a hair from an owl's feather, or a strong vulture's feather, and place that hair on the pain, until the purple circle surrounds the entire area; then bring your hand back to the end of the hair until you feel all around the pain, and put it in place, and scrape the pain from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, so make this of a dog's or a horse's head according to this form, and be subtle and draw across:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	And if you see, so make this of a dog's or a horse's head according to this form, and be subtle and draw across: ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser And cauterize the fire, so as it is in front or chapiter of cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the cloister
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	No clister of silver or archaut, or melted bronze or brass is made; and no instrument is made small or large, according to the uses to which it is put.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	So as to be brought for the treatment of children who are weak and painful, they are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the cloister is small and large above [the head], or the belly is tied according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and I say there is a gap where the belly is tied together, so that you see it, and the chiseled sides are pierced inside; and one of the two has a hole, and the other; and the belly where someone puts medicines from a bladder or parchment, and pierce all around the small holes, and put between each hole an inch of space, then pour into these holes a strong wire thread twisted in X or in twine wrapped around, and tie the belly together as if it were a sheep; and when the medicine is inside, if he binds the instrument in front of a strong thread, then bless; and this is the shape of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and oil or olive oil or some similar thing is applied to the clister; then pour it lightly; then the ministers spread their hands together, until they are completely wet, then remove the clister, and place the patient's legs against the wall, and let the medicine come out as much as possible; and if he sleeps a whole night, it is greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you plaster him with plasters when he is sick from a decay of the abdomen, and the medicine quickly comes out, then remind him until he is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are in the foundation or an abscess, then the plaster is also as thin as for a child; and this is the form of the thin plaster where the skin is stretched:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have said in the division the cure of wounds; or we will tell you the cures of hands and medicines, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are various according to what they are made, and according to the places or wounds are made, and of how they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by hitting a stone, and a size of an axe or a mace or a spear or a fust or a lance or a sledgehammer, or similar things; or that are made according to the places of the body, so as a wound that strikes on the neck, or on the head, or on the side, or on the stomach, or on the liver, and similar limbs; and I will tell you the cure of each wound, and will begin with simple head wounds, for the reminder will come in his plaster.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes where the head is, and the bone is not broken, take care if it is from movement of stone or similar things, and the skin is nonetheless torn and the wound is great, and you doubt about the temperature: if you do this quickly healing from the head itself if it comes little blood from the wound, and let the healing be opposite to the wounded part; and refuse the patient's repletion of wine and fatty meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	I say that if it does not heal, if its meat is wasting, and it does not drink wine, nor does it eat cheese; and put on the wound, if it is hot, wet with oil and dry up a little; or, if it is cold, wet with wine that makes it stiff; and if there is no heat in it, if it is fresh all over, and is not moved by the wind, powder, which I will say a little later; and if it has been moved, put on some onions, until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is great as of a sword's blade and similar, and the lips cannot be joined by tenons, if they are joined by sewing, as I will say to the wounds of the belly, from the seam.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	And if the wound is exposed to the bone and it can only hold for one punch, then wrap it with leather tightly; instruct the patient to eat large meat, as well as baked bread and similar foods.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find dry rot on the leather and it has not reached the bone, then cut it off completely and burn it, then treat it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which, without bandaging, cannot be stopped by medicine, then tie the artery, and if that does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the cure is light: and it is that you put this powder which hardens so that fire has moved.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the way of the powder is this: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; live chalts three parts, and powder it finely, and apply the wound, and bind it together, until it has healed well and joined together all its blood; and then bind it firmly, and leave it untied if it swells; for we do not use medicine as long as it is healthy.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never do we use any of the chalts alone, when we have not incense nor dragon' s blood, but that fire has moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if fire has moved the wound, at most it is still wet, but put on any of these medicines: or eggs of eggs yolks cooked in wine or honey, until it has dried out; and then heal with other remedies as long as it is healthy.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with fine pincers; and I will tell you about fractures of the head next.
de la plaie dou col	from the neck wound,
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	the wound comes from the neck and it is simple, if there is no difference between it and that of the head, but the neck where the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the neck, if there is no other device than to let it heal, and not put anything restricting, because it harms the neck and makes it retreat; and do not put anything on the wound, because the substance of the neck is cold, and its continuation is with the skull, which is the highest member; but be the medicine sweet, if like hot water in cold water, and mix it with oil of roses, and wash it too in cold water, and other pebbles of mining according to this way, and wet them with oil.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then the cure as long as it is healthy.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and the bowels are full of blood, then the piercing or more deeply; and if the artery is cut, and bleeding comes from it, so that it becomes dark, and the wound is washed, and cauterized as above; and if the spitting in the throat is cut, or the voice, and the conduct is guarded, so that meat goes well, if the cure is made on the chin of the throat, and not touching the throat but sets it according to its natural form; and then binds it forward, and leaves it for some days, then cures with ointments that are useless as long as it is healthy; and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, then search for it; and if there are pieces of bone, if you can reach them all, and those you cannot reach, leave them until the wound putrefies and is cured and the issue goes out; and if the wound is fresh, then sprinkle the powder that I said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones in the wound, and there is a fistula, then treat it as I said in my chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a lance or a knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from a lance or a knife, and the wound is deep, then look out for windiness in the patient: since then the wound is fatal; and if it is not deep and is fresh throughout its length, then do not put on powder at all, nor bind it so that it does not come apart, but let it rest against the wound, and wrap it up, but if you have no ointment, put raw wool in the wound to absorb the moisture, and let the patient lie down on the wound for three days, or four, or more; then he will not get spasms or a bad shake from the body's reaction; and when you see the bones in position, then know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Cure the boils and other cures, as long as it is healthy; and if it cannot heal, then suture that there is a fistula; so the cure as it should be.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife, and it is simple, deep or on the back, then heal with this; if it is large, stitch it; and if it is small, use powder, and if it has broken into the bone, and there are pieces, then cut the wound, and the sharp ones if they are caught; and if they are not caught, then let the wound pus, so ease the extractions; and for other wounds to other members, the judgment is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	Dou derrompement du ventre
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The rupture of the abdomen is great and small, and there are many wounds; therefore the intestine often comes out, or the intestines come out, for which the incision is made; and the stitch is less difficult, and there is no more pain in a small wound than in a large one, so that we place them back again from hot to hot; for this reason the intestines swell sometimes when they feel cold, so we place them back again, and because they are worse for a small wound, whereas we hold them back at their own level, so that they are not worse. And know that the rupture of the abdomen is according to three ways: the common stitches come out in the stitch of the abdomen, and the stitch of other wounds comes out in other places; and yet they are more proper with the stitch of the abdomen, and I will tell you each one and I will explain it.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing from the intestines has come out, and there is no need to hurry, this should be done in one of two ways: or because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen by cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, heat it in one of the two ways: moisten a sponge or a thin cloth entirely with lukewarm water, or cook it in warm squinant and cumin and spice, and draw out the intestines as much as they swell; and never stop doing this, and rest, that you may cool down.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling go away, if you moisten the intestines with water or warm it and boil herbs, because this keeps the entrance closed to a small amount; and if it cannot enter, if you make a small cut in the wound with the instrument with which we cut hemorrhoids; and the first cure is to rest that we do not cut unless there is great necessity; and this is the tool for splitting: if you cut inside the core and take it away, and see how it looks like this.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged and the intestines are loose, if you reset it according to its natural form in its proper place, for this is worth doing, because otherwise it will not heal.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	And when the wound is large and in the part of the loins of the belly, it is fitting that you make the patient lie on his back, and raise his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the part of the loins of the belly, then raise the head and the chest higher than the parts of the loins, and so the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts, and so you arrange it that what I said about large and small wounds applies.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, you should arrange it so that the patient lies on his side, and then place your hands between them to minister to the rupture with your fingers; and gather the lips together. This is the common way of suturing, and it is that you press a needle or more, according to the quantity of the largeness of the wound, and then leave two inches from the edge of the wound on top, and stick a needle through both ends of the skin, as far as you can get it into that part, and gather the two sides of the skin together; then draw a double thread around the needle from both sides, and gather the two edges of the wound together, and then leave an inch or so, and stick in another needle; then lead the second thread around the first needle, as you did with the first, until all the wound is closed; and let the needles be medium size, fine and coarse, for the fine needles will go through the whole skin, and the too coarse ones cannot enter well: therefore they should be of medium size; and do not push the needles too far away from the skin and the cuir, lest they break the skin and open the wound before it is sutured; and then tie off the ends of the thread, so that the patient does not scratch himself in his sleep, and I cover the needle ends with cloth or blankets to hold them in place, and leave them until the wound has healed. This way of sewing with needles is more convenient for small wounds, for if you sewed with a single stitch, you should gather the two sides of the skin and the two edges of the wound together with one needle or thread, and sew them together as you would cut cloth; and then leave an inch or so between each stitch, the length of a smaller finger; this stitch is good for men, and I sewed up a wound that had once been cut by a knife, which was naverted [ruptured] from one side of the abdomen to the other, and it was torn open by the intestines, which were as wide as two fingers, and the wound was in the middle of the abdomen;
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought the intestine back; then it had been for 22 hours outside, and it was sewed up after 15 days, and I healed it, and it was healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the mirth had told me that he was dying, and it was a miracle; and I did not heal it with any ointment, for I was in a place where there was no ointment to be found, nor any medicines; and I put on cotton wool twice a day on the wound, and washed it with honey water until it was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or I will tell you the two ways of stitching: take the needle and dip it from the outside to the inside; when it has pierced through the middle, so that the thread of the right side matches up with the thread on the other side, then tie it off; this is how one should stitch, just as the fur-dresser does when he stitches fur, and you should leave the hook on one side, and bring it back to the other, until the stitching is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second way of sewing, which Galen did properly, is if it is so that there is no thread, which joins the two parts together naturally, and applies one of the heads to the other head in this manner: take a needle or thread from the next head, and make it go through the bottom, leaving the two heads together; then turn the needle, and make it go through from the outside part up to that inside, across the two heads; then make it go through the one and the other from the outside part up to that inside, in two other heads that are on the other side; and this is the muddled way of sewing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	And Galen did so say, and no one testified, that you should sew the belly to two needles, or there is a thread in each; and you must push one needle from one side, and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew rope; and know that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly, this sewing is more painful than any other belly sewing.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l'ait muee, si remet arer l'intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l'ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu'il soit sanez; et se tu n'as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu'ele comance a giter bowe, coton veel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k'il soit sanez.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	If the wound is fresh and the arrow has gone through it, remove the Arrow, and cut off the hair around it; then apply powder mixed with water and oil to the wound, and bind it with string and poultice; and if the wound begins to hurt or ooze, often dip a light cloth in wine, and wash it over the wound; and if it is an arrow that has entered deeply, the wound will ooze blood and pus; and know that when the large intestine is injured, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestinal stuff called "jejunum" can't heal when it's still attached, and that's because of the way veins are planted, and because of the whole body's subtlety, and its resemblance to babies.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	If the lump jumps out of the wound, put it back in like the intestin, while it's still fresh; and if it's old and turned brown, you need to find the spot that's black, since there are veins and arteries; then cut what's between the two bones, and hang them from the side of the wound all the way to the back so that the extraction can happen when the lump jumps out, and the wound will close.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture in the bowel
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestin is ripped and the wound is small, you can restore it in some places, since I've seen that some good ones were navered or pierced by a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became wrapped up and turned into a fistula, and that's where the excretion and wind came out; I applied treatment according to what I could find, and I didn't stop being subtle until it healed, and I sewed up the leaks.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	Et when I saw it sewn up, I doubted that the patient had done him harm in his belly; and there was no harm, but tarried in better dispositions, and eating and drinking; and none of the experimenters said that when he has a small wound in the intestine, that he must be tied up in some manner: take fibres from big testicles, then bring together the lips of the wound, and when the fibres have opened the mouth, put it on II lips, so that she pulls her mouth up; and then li takes his head, and that is so that he cannot release it, and then puts another fibre after in that manner before, until the wound is all taken; and let the wound go.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	And if it burns in the intestine, and does no harm to the patient, and can be tied up with a thin thread cut from the intestine of an animal in some manner: take the end of that thread that is slightly severed, then tie the end of that thread to the end of a fine twisted linen thread, then sew the thread into the intestine, and cut it off at the tear; and this method of sewing with fibres is no more than according to the way of faith and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, most certainly when it is in one of the small intestinal grooves, there is no cure except subtility.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	for the fistula so that it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	I know that all wounds and abscesses, once they have healed, are called 'fistula' in general terms, and most especially when they have furrowed the skin and become a bowstring.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	I know that all wounds and abscesses, once they have healed, are called 'fistula' in general terms, and most especially when they have furrowed the skin and become like a bowstring; and there is never any clear popping sound, nor is there ever any pain, it is as if there were no wound. Nor has it been cured, and I have not spoken of the division of wounds, that all wounds which are not healed are due to one of the VIII causes: namely, the smallness of the vein or artery; or its evil nature; or because there is something hard inside, under the lips, so that it does not let a hole form; or too much bowels; or the part is rotten and the substance is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in the cure; or because it is like pestilence in the region; or because digestion is late and health is slow to arrive and escapes by nature; or there are veins or bones: I have already described all these causes, signs, and cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is fitting that I make you aware of the treatment for fistula, which is achieved by handiwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Fistulas can occur in all limbs of the body; for there are fistulas that come from great veins, and arteries, and nerves, or to the sinus, or intestine, or bladder, or some of the ribs, or spine of the back, or any joint of the hands or feet; and if it comes that it enters into the proper limb, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are in this manner are of great difficulty, and there is only work and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come to the limb's main place, and similar places, then it must be cured, and you have begun to cure it, and you have recognized it, then take a tent of iron or steel, if the fistula is straight, seek it; and if the fistula is twisted, seek it with a thin tent of lead, for the lead bends around the twists; and if the fistula has broken hands, and you cannot cure it well with tents, then cauterize it with fire, for fire corrupts it so that it no longer hurts; and then cure it thoroughly, as far as you can, then put medicine in a tent that is moistened with water, and bottle it up to the top of the fistula, until the medicine corrupts the excess that is reserved at the bottom; and then put oignons that are rotten between the clean ones, as much as it is cured; and if it is not cured by this, then cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then cauterize it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If in the neck there is a pain or injury to the main members as we have said; and if the jaw is dislocated, and there is corruption and darkening, so long as the corruption is all bone, then treat with medicine until it is healthy; and if it is not healthy, and it returns as before, knowing that you have not yet reached the root: if you discover and seek until you are at the bottom, and take away all the corruption, then restore the joint; and if it is healthy in this way, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If this does not work, know that the corruption is too complete that you cannot come to it; if there is no other defect but to allow nature to act; and if there is one small corrupted bone, and you can pull it out with pliers, if you extract it with the right tool for this, and if there are many bones, then break them all, and do not leave any; and if moisture makes you wrong, and there is no mistake or fear, take off and wet and heat, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you do not remove them in an hour, place over the wound something that causes putrefaction, and let it be as long as the pus is between the bones, and then the bones will come out more easily; and if it is a large bone, such as of the leg or thigh, wait so much for corruption until all the bone is blackened, then patch up the wound; and if there is a great deal of corruption and it has come to the root of the bone, if it is worth and cover everything up to the corruption, and then cure it until it is healed; and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you can take examples and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	Here is the first sentence of the text: "Et si tu ne les pois oster a une houre," si mets sur la plaie chose enjanrant pourriture, et laisse tant que li luis soit pourris entre les os, et adonc si avront plus legerement les os; et si c'est un gros os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis retoure la plaie; et s'il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient juscy a mole de l'os; si le convient soier et coper tout juscy a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu'il soit soudez.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I placed a tent over one of these openings, and then searched all the openings and found that one came against the other on all sides of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I rushed then, and covered one of the openings as much as I could discover part of the bone, and found that it was corroded and pierced, and the corruption extended all the way inside the bone; I knew what appeared to me to be the bone's corruption, and took care that there was no other corruption than that which I discovered; and then I began to treat the wound with medicines for a long time, and could not mend it; and then I began again, and discovered the bone just as before, and found the continuing corruption in the bone, and knew it, and then I took out the bone, and leaned over it so that I could mend the joint; but I couldn't because I covered it with one palm of the bone, and I put it back together with medicines; and it healed and was mended firmly, and I didn't need to reopen the wound except for the weakness of the sick person, who couldn't bear it, and for the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	Car for the evacuation of blood happened often, but he was healed entirely, and gave birth to the bone a hard shell, and was of good temper and had no harm or contrary from all to all, nor to air nor to come.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	If the bone is broken in any place of the trunk, then it shall be in this way: take a thong, and stretch it to the head of the bone that is open, and command no one that he should extend it upwards; and put another thong of larger size than the first thong, and fasten it to the shell that is over the bone, and untie the thong, so that you pull the broken shell off the bone, and uncover the shell on the place where you see and feel the corruption, and fasten again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open up, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, then uncover the whole charnel; then place a hot brand on it, and then thread the corruption from one part to the other, and let the thread hang down from the length of the corruption, as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut off the joint that is corrupted, and thread the bone or what is in its place; and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, then there is no other injury but that of the coper; and if the corruption is at the knuckle of the hand or at the knuckle of the foot, then this is very bad, but it is necessary that you inquire about this corruption, how it opens up; and purify it in all ways that you can, but so that the vein or nerve do not make it opposite; and know that the saw and the threads for capping these bones are many, according to the appearance of the bones and their size and subtility and greatness and smallness and hardness; and for this reason it is necessary to arrange each tool according to its form, and know that the work will show you the tool that you need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the signs of the ways of diseases; so consider the tool that you have need of according to what is appropriate.
dou feu	Fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	When the shoulder is dislocated by pressure or from falling, and when you have applied medicine to this corrosion with cures of medicines, and it does not benefit, then cover that member to the place where the corrosion comes, so that the patient escapes from this death, or from the evil, which is greater, of the defect of the member; and the signs are that the members become black, as though they were burned by fire, and this corrosion spreads from one member to another, and penetrates all over the body; if you hurry to cover it, and if it is by the stinging of certain poisonous animals, such as sea scorpions and weasels and similar things, then cover it quickly, for it does not give space to come up to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes up to the hand, then cover it at the joint, so that the corrosion does not come up to the arm; and if it comes to the arm, then cover it at the shoulder; and if it passes the shoulder, it is death, and there is no remedy but the quantity of its virtue; and do this whenever the corrosion appears or progresses: if it comes to the first joint, then cover after the other joint; and if it comes or progresses down, then cover all the way down; and if it comes up in the leg, then cover at the joint of the knee; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy but to make the sick person die; and the manner of covering or weaving the member is that you bind it above and below with one minister's thread and another minister's thread, and you loosen the band which is between the two threads at a wide spatumile, as much as the bone is uncovered; then cover or weave, and put a linen cloth on each side, so that the weave does not touch the healthy part, and comes to the sick person another injury and abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if the pain comes when you work, then cauterize the place well, or put on some restraining powders; then return to your medicine until it is complete, then bind the injured member with a suitable bandage, and heal it until it is well; and I will tell you what happened to the man at home in a moment: he got a blackness that looked like fire had burned him, and that corrosion came first on his foot, so that it hurt all his foot; and when the man saw the corrosion, then he covered his foot with copper, and he healed; and long after that the corrosion returned to the palm of his hand, and came to me, and I put things that reflect after cleansing the skin, and I could not stop the corrosions; and he said that I should cut off his hand, and I did not want to, because I had hope of reflexing the material; and I also doubted that if I would cut off his hand, he would not die, for the man's virtue was weak; and he despaired all, and returned to his land, and covered his hand with copper, and he healed; and I have only told you because there is another way that they might do this, if it is necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	No times comes abscess in the middle of a charred meat, and lasts so long that it makes a big bunch of bowels; then it rips and perforates, and jumps the bowels, and remains the viscera shut, just as our servants do; and the leather which is above it is also very thin like the drapes we unravel, and does not corrode until it reaches the bone, nor until the nerve, and such a disease is called "healthy", and is not called "fistula"; but if it has grown so long that it reaches the bone in full, then it is called "fistula"; and the leather which is above it, you should cut all this leather, and most especially when it is thin like our drapes; and does not harm for its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you think that the leather is getting redder, and the corruption has not yet reached its full extent, and the leather is charred like a brand, then apply this: take medicine from ancient Egypt which is made in this way: take equal parts of oil, and resin, and chalk, and put them in a vase on the fire until the medicine becomes red, and also thickens; and then take some of it according to your need, and make an ointment with honey and water, and apply it to the breast, and strain the medicine out; leave it for two hours, then squeeze it out; do this many times until the breast is completely white, and the pus comes out; and never use water from ashes when this medicine is not present, but take ashes from a vine stalk, and pour water on them, then boil it, and make an ointment with it, until you know that the breast has become completely white; and if the patient cannot bear the medicine, or the Egyptian medicine, or the water of ashes, then make an ointment with honey and wine which is slightly sweetened, so that the property of honey to whiten and wash is present, and the wine makes it bitter; and when you have done this, and know that the breast has become completely white, if the hole from which the milk comes out is small, and the catheter cannot enter, then make it a little wider with an iron tool, and put it in a tent of the Egyptian ointment, or basilicon ointment, until it becomes wider; and if the wound is too wide, leave it open to the air where the catheter can enter, and if the hole from which the milk comes out is at the top, then cut it higher or lower than that place.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	Car when the bowels are in perfect health, they should not be disturbed; and if you cannot cover the navel as you see fit, prepare it in such a way that the bowels run down to the lowest part that they are, for when the bowels are in perfect health, they should not be disturbed and if you cannot cover the navel as you see fit, prepare it in such a way: that the bowels run lightly downward, leaving nothing of the bowel; and take medicines that solidify it over the navel, and place them on I linene drape that covers all of the navel; then cover at the lower part of the navel with a thin piece of linen according to the quantity of the opening, and place it over the navel to support the bowel, and do not remove the large drape until after many days once; and those who are on the navel opening should often remove it to remove the bowel, and know what runs from the bowel, whether it is venom or pus or enough or digested or indigestive; and take care if the patient feels pain or no, and if there is an abscess or not, and how your medicine has spread in such a way that you see the nature rise over the navel opening, know that the breasts have begun to move, and approach them with care; and then remove it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you remove the wound, if you change another drape, and renew the dressing.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if her breasts become swollen and uncomfortable after many days, know that her breasts are not yet developed.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons remain in the body for a long time, do not despair of health, because health approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are some who delay the healing of wounds, and others who do the opposite; and if breast swelling persists for many days, know that the breasts have not yet developed; and if the breasts are late to mature, and seem to be drawing back, then prepare medicine by mixing a mixture of vinegar and oil, and dry it in the sun; then grind it and use it; or, make honey with it as follows: take mirr, aloe and incense, and grind them together, and add wine; then use it as a paste, and apply it to the breast; and never give it as an infusion, for if you do, you will cause great harm, and this is because corruption begins to spread in the bones, or in the limbs, and this is what causes healing to be delayed, and not to be healed with this medicine, so know that complete corruption has set in, and has caused a pressure in the bone, or in the limb; if the cure of the fistula is delayed, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the toenail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	A bunion is an aposteme that arises from the nail of the hand or foot, or perhaps in another two; and when it has become deformed, and we do not take care, then it becomes a bunion that runs and corrodes and breaks down the root of the nail, and perhaps it corrupts all; and there is a corrosion to the bone, so much that there is a painful and pungent pain, and the two bones are wide apart, and the color is pale.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the cure does not profit, then you must cut off all the surplus that is reserved of the nail, and then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cauterization is a great help if the bone is healthy, and the nail is healthy too; and if the nail presses the flesh and begins to prick it, and bleeds, then you must cut off the nail that pricks the flesh, and cut it high, and trim the tip of the nail carefully and lightly, and put on the remaining part of the nail burning and corrosive remedies to destroy it all; and then treat with ointments until it is healthy.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	Et si la corrosion est dans l'os, alors il doit être taillé et traité avec force, car tant que l'os est corrompu, il ne peut guérir ; et si tu vois la déformation, alors tu dois le guérir autant qu'il est possible de le faire sain ; et s'il est blessé et enflé, et sent une grande douleur, alors il convient que tu le guérisses d'abord ; puis taie l'ongle avec un scie obtenir en coupant à travers au-dessus, et veille à ce que la coupe n'aille pas jusqu'à la chair qui est au-dessus de l'ongle, car le malade ressentirait une douleur excessive ; et s'il arrive, alors mets quelque chose sur lui qui apaise.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	la douleur du sourdoyer de la main
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.
