Il faut soutenir ce qui naît dans les mains de certains hommes par accident est tout charnu, et par accident il a un os, et aucune fois il a une onglet, et aucun d'eux naissent à la racine de la jointure, ou la naissance est dans certains de nous des deux.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Cil who is born between two limbs do not move, and cil who is born at the joint of two limbs, by chance they move; the size of the one who is charnus is so light in a certain way: cut it in its root with a wide chisel.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Cil who is born at the root of the joint must be carefully treated: if you have any doubt, take care.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the one who is born or must be cut at the derrien nout, it is necessary that you first chop the fat roundly up to the bone, then chop the bone with a suitable thread and then cure it as long as it is healthy.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The joints that come together by birth, or by jointing a wound, or by fire burning, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	If you doubt that you have properly jointed the jointure, so that it repairs itself according to its natural forms; then place between two towels or drapelets soaked in oil and rosin, so that it does not joint; or place between two pieces of fine cloth, until the joints are healed, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.
des vils	If the wound comes between the two palms, then wipe it as it should be done.
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	The vis are thickly coated with a melancholy waste that comes from the core members of the body; and there is more in the legs of those who walk on their feet and work and carry loads, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you must not perform any cleansing of the wound, and then heal it from the base.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The cure with iron is according to two ways: one is that it is wiped, and the black blood is drawn out; and the other way is that you let the wound ooze all its blood.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The size of the incision is according to this manner: arise the first the leg of hot water very much, until the gross blood is thinned, then extract the leg of the ill person from above the knee down to the shin; and wipe the wound in one, two or three places, with a wide incision, then drain and draw out the black blood by hand, from one end to another, as much as the virtue of the ill person can bear; and then bandage it, and order him to blacken his meat by rubbing with black ink; and restart the evacuation and healing when the wounds are clean, and wash the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is found in the legs, in warm parts where no herbs or trees grow, and in the ground where there is no moisture; and by chance it may grow elsewhere than in the legs, and this leads to the skin's decay that comes from within the body, spiraling like a snake, digging between skin and bone.

des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	vers that are born between leather and cart
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our country "buff disease" because it often affects buffaloes, and it is a small worm that is born between leather and cart, and goes up and down all over the body, breaking through the skin wherever it goes, and causes putrefaction of some humors, as worms and snails and insects and larvae; and one may doubt its malice, for when it goes through the body, and comes to the head, and enters the oil, it may turn back, and destroy the oil; and this often happens.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you view it to heal and extract, if you can only do so when he goes: then it is necessary that you place the joint above and tight with a strong knot, then cope on and draw it hard, and let it fall perfectly into the cart, and you don't find out, then cauterize him with fire as soon as he dies; and the greatest damage he does is that he runs oil, just like we said; and if you see him come where the head is near the oil, then pull off his sack tightly, then cope on and draw it hard. de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	from pain which comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called in our language "vakirir", and it is a pain which comes to some members, and because of which one member moves to another; and I have seen this which I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and I uncovered her arms, and saw a little swelling in the veins of the arms; and immediately it went up as high as a worm in the shoulder, more quickly than anything else, so that it felt like a piece of silver when it passed from one place to another; the pain left that place, and entered into the shoulder, and then after a short while corrupted throughout the whole body, until she came to the other arm. Then she told me that she was twisting herself around the body, just as I saw her.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marvelled at how this woman moved from one member to another, for I had never seen such a disease in this way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Nevertheless, I had never seen anyone with such a disease move from one member to another before; I thought that perhaps this was why the woman's body was so rigid and her veins were exposed, and also because of the constant twitching she seemed to be doing; and I didn't rule out the fact that those who are luxurious, and have moist bodies and veiny arms that are covered up, might experience such a thing.

And when you treat this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if he opens like we have said, let him lie on his back and rest comfortably in that position; then cauterize the site; and if you do not see blood at the wound, treat with pills that stop the bleeding, with serapin pills, and similar remedies.
des saiettes	arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	are various, according to their appearances and according to the places of their impact on the body.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	have different shapes, some with large tips, others with small, some with feathers, some welded, and some with two angles, some with tongues, and some with pieces; and some pierce in any member differently: or in a principal member they pierce, as the brain, heart, liver, stomach, intestines, bladder, and similar organs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie. Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent. And the sign of a seizure when it starts is that there is no foam from the wound, and the throat swells, and the color of the patient changes, and he gasps and makes a loud noise.

The patient who is cured of disease does not have a determined heat, but when the time comes for it or for food, in all hours and at all times; and it is not appropriate for the doctor to cure children until they are 12 or 13 years old, nor women who have been pregnant for only four months until they reach seven months.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	Do not cure the old people who have passed sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	If you are going to cure anyone, in whatever way, it is appropriate to have them drink a light clistere if they have diarrhea, or if they have held back pee, so that the intestines do not draw out the harmful waste that hurts the main members; and it is not appropriate to cure someone who is too swollen from meat, or who is bloated, as much as possible, or yawners; and if there is a passion of colic, vomiting, cramping of the belly, and frequent urination due to having many sexual partners, and staying up late, and eating, drinking, and taking medicines, then it is appropriate to cure them, but slowly; then take a bath or a dip, unless something helps them, to subtilize their heat, and make them well from the vein at the back of the knee on the third day, as we have said; and guard yourself from that work, and from eating late, and lust, and similar things; and be strict and disciplined, and let the healer who heals you be higher than the one who is healing; and rub your arms twice or three times, then pull the cord with a little force because if it is too tight or too loose, it cannot be fixed; and then rub the healer with your left hand on the vein where you are going to cure, a little at a time, until the veins swell and can be felt; then moisten the healer with the flame of a small drop of old oil, then put your thumb of your left hand on that vein where you are going to cure, so that the vein does not hurt and feel it; then rub your right arm with your left hand a little at a time until the veins swell and can be felt.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that run like strings for the sailor, and if they are such that they are prone to windiness, so when one puts them on the flame, then removes the flame, and cannot open the vein, then they are of this type; and if he opens the vein, then the wound is too narrow, so it is necessary that the sailor be warned of these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens the first time, it is good; but if not, then begin again a little more of that same medicine or on hospital, if the leeches are not swelled.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the leeches are swollen and the patient seems to improve, let him rest for a day or two, and do not tie his arm: perhaps he will get abscesses; do not put them on the flame, but begin the treatment again if it pleases you; and if the wound is small, or there is little blood flowing subtly and you doubt whether it will flow as much as you see, then set the fire directly on the wound; and do a little hospital work, so that the leeches are swollen. For this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see a vein burst, do not warn the patient, and put a little oil on it, for it smooths the path of the blood, and the oil is soft in this place; and thus administer the oil to each vein that you heal the veins with, so as to stop the flow of blood; and the same does triaicle and bowels of ewe when put on top of the area; but if it is too thick, it will split so carefully.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	If you see a large abscess, which often happens, especially when the opening of the vein is small, hurry and put a moist sponge on top, and tie it tightly for an hour; and it is necessary that you do this after the exit of the blood from the vein, and if it remains in place after some days there is no harm, but if you see it, put any of aloe or mirr on the juice of calamus, mint, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times there was an abscess and appearance at the base of the thigh: so put your hand on it, and if you find the soft part under pressure from the hand, then this appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid putting anything on this that we have said, because perhaps in cutting through the artery; but dry it with poultice to harden the place, then treat it with other treatment until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each wound according to the quantity of its virtue and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the wound is black, let it out until it is red; and if you see the lump large, let it out until it is thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And for those who are flat and foreign, and need to extract blood, let them make a larger wound and wide flames; and for those who are weak, do the opposite, and heal them little by little, and cut them across, not cutting them forward; and this way of healing is saved from the decay of blood and the swelling of nerves, and it is better than long healing.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for those whose course is towards sickness, it is necessary to give damp bread in grape juice; if it is heated, if it suffers from three or four times of wind and gas, and if it has a cold complexion, if it is served before the sick dry bread in syrup of muscat, or in honey syrup aromatized with spices, as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and dates, and well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if it has a fever at the beginning of illness, after the exit of the wind of the sick, it is necessary that it smells brew of wine and subtle odorless syrup, and uses other things that we have said in the division or chapter of syncope for the evacuation of the vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if it vomits up one arm and sickens another at times, when it is weakened by great sickness, that it be healed little by little according to the quantity of its continuing virtue.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who vomits up his arms after the first hour, and he has a strong heart, if he is sick for seven hours after the first hour, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who vomits up elsewhere, if he must vomit the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For he has blood coming up from within the body which heats him and brings fever; if so much comes out, and the opening is enlarged to the point that it chokes him, then you should treat all conditions of vomiting, and put your hand on his pulse when he vomits, lest death come to him in a fit, and this happens often, as long as he neglects to treat the vomiting; and do not break the shoulder when you see it dislocated, and bring up the blood the second time, and close the opening, that you press hard upon it; nor if it is broken, let him stretch his arm out widely, for that would be wrong, but leave it until he vomits the second time; or you may point to the tip of the flame, as long as the blood which comes up is frozen at the opening of the vein, and put a piece of string dipped in water on it, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein has burst, leave it alone and do not restrain it, as long as the abscess is quiet.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to drain blood a second time, let it be done in the same place or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein that runs through the arm is tied at the base of the vein from which blood flows, so that it does not flow further.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the way of tying this vein is that the patient holds his hand in hot water until it turns red; then let it rest gently so that the vein appears clearly, then tie it now across, neither wide nor long; and if the cut is wide, tie it close to the joint of the hand, and do not remove it again, unless it comes loose, then put the hand back in hot water and let the blood run in the water as long as you have enough; and if it has come loose, do not re-tie the hand in hot water, for we tie it more in haste than in rest; and the tying of this vein is more safe from all other veins than if there were no arteries or nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	The treatment for a liver disease with the right hand is as follows: stretch out the hand, and dip it in hot water until the vein disappears if you can see it; and then twist the hand around, and cut off all of it at once, unless it hurts anything; and don't cut too much at once, because the nerves are all exposed and bare, and then put the hand back into hot water, so that it does not get frozen in the wound, and cannot be taken out.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The doctor will treat the patient's disease with fire cauterization on his left hand, and you should do the same for the right hand as I have instructed you.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The treatment for the patient's disease of the shoulder should be applied to all other diseases that affect the body, such as those affecting the arm, and also to pain in the back, legs, and feet, and similar ailments.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	For the quality of the treatment for the patient's shoulder disease, it is that the patient should dip his affected part in hot water, and rub it on the vein until it heals, and then apply it to the joint of the foot; and if the vein is at the ankle, and then many rains go up the leg; heal the rain, or more rain, or at the ankle, that it may move.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you treat the patient's foot, be careful of the nails that grow out, and also treat it by walking as if climbing stairs, and let the flames go out.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if it cannot come out on its own, put the foot into water, and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if he needs to be resected for the first time, begin again for the second time above a little on top because the joint is salty; do not doubt about the nerves, as we have said, and thus make the surgery of the other leg even.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The joint of the sciatic vein is at the ankle and its resection is worth the pain in the hip when it comes to bloodletting.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of this resection is that the patient goes into or bath, and extracts from the ankle IIII with twisting, because otherwise it does not open; and if it opens, do so in all ways that you can, and going over; and it is worth more to cut than let it be, for the joint is out, and it is very reponsive to hand.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not [set it] straight, so that there is no rain from him who opens or closes the foot, and towards the little finger, and guard against the nerves; and make so much blood flow that you see, and then loosen the ligature, and put on cotton and bind it; now he is healed.
des sainies de ventouse	vessels for sucking up
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	are made from horns, or leather, or glass; and ventilation is done in two ways: either by hurting and drawing blood, or without hurting.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this ventilation which is without hurting is in XIIII parts of the body, so that one is all in the head; and others are under the neck; and II others on the two sides of the neck; and the windpipe is behind the throat; and the windpipes are at the two arms; and the windpipes of the two legs; and the windpipes of the two ankles; and ventilation does not deal with blood, except for small veins that are scattered in the body, and therefore it does not matter if they are all opened or some of them are left closed, as is done with a sucking cup; and it should be adjusted only to those who have an excess of food and drink, so that all their bodies are emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	Et s'il est nécessaire à cause de maladie ou d'habitude, nous devons les faire ventouser toutes les heures pendant le mois, ou à la fin, et au milieu de chaque temps ; car il y a de tels qui, lorsqu'ils ont besoin de ventouser, sont très lourds ; et ceux qui ont une forte haleine et des rougeurs sur leur visage, leur chef, leur cou et des ténèbres dans les yeux ; et ceux qui ont une goutte de sang dans leur bouche et la langue enflée, et qui boivent du sang ; et s'il y a de tels qui rêvent, et voient par manque de nourriture et de boisson et de mort et de choses semblables.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we saw these signs, and especially when it is mid-month, we order them to ventouse after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The medicament of the fever with aid to the greiness of the head… which comes to the hairs, and cannot come but after the evacuation of all the body; and this ventilation is in the place of the medicament of the cephalical, and cannot come but to those who are of a cold disposition and use it, or who have a chattering, for this does them much harm; and therefore it cannot come but to the old in using, nor to those who have cold diseases in their heads.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who recover from it often become confused, and for this the suction cup must be placed a little further downstream due to the doubt of confusion.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The ventilation of the neck is in the place of the healing of the head and the basilica, and therefore it causes stretching of the chest, and a cut in the throat, and vomiting; and therefore it should be released little by little, for if it holds too tight, it brings confusion or stomach trouble or anything else.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The winds at the back of the chest as the pain in the head, and it blinding and migraine, and strangulation, and pain in the roots of the teeth, and is in the place of the health of the temple; and it is necessary that you instruct the doctor that he presses his hand with a putty, that he does not grip the artery, and does not cause the flow of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The winds at the back of the mouth as disease in the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and is in the place of health of the lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The winds at the shoulders as disease that comes from heat and filling up.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The winds at the arms as much as three veins in the arms, because it draws blood from these large veins; and instruct the doctor that he does not cut too deeply, for their bones are bare, and they know how to cut nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The ventouse that is on the back so suits to emoroid of the fundament, and to maladies desoz, and it convents that the ventouse be big, and be of air, that she has need of well traire; and per adventure, if she were subtilz, she would break; and she makes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The leg ventouses so open, for they draw blood from all the body, and suit to ancient pains of the hips, and of the feet, and of the bladder, and put back the flowers; and are in place of the two knees, and the two ankles, but weaken the body greatly after long use, and bring death in many conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way of putting the ventouse is that you put it first empty, and suck quickly, and place it carefully, and move evenly, and do not cease to do this as long as you see the red and inflamed place, and appear the pain of blood; then set fire, and remove the ventouses, and take care in the disposition of the bodies, for there are such who have great fever, and thin pores: so it convents to wound once only, and to make deep wounds, and a hole by depths; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if he is thin outside, he must strike twice: once to make the blood thinner,
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if he is very fat outside, he must strike the third time; and when we want to squeeze out blood little by little, we only need to press once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want to squeeze blood out, let us start again often; and if he is fat outside, he must be struck completely, and the end is such that the pulse stops suddenly, and he covers himself with an oil that opens and dissolves: if it is in spring, use violet oil or sweet almond oil or pumpkin seed oil; and if it is in summer, use watercress oil, lily oil, chamomile oil, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if it is swollen and cold, take oil of amber, or of balm, or of anise, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if it is sore to the touch and large pores, there is no need to put oil on it, but it should be washed after the wind-bath with rose water, or cold water, or water of mulberries, or water of cucumbers, or water of porcelain, or otherwise.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And if it is wet with moisture, if it comes up with this, or with water of myrtle, and of sumach, and of similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And if they have swollen swollen parts, they are raised with old wine, or with water of oak, or with a decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar things; and they should not be treated with the vacuum before or during the bath, but after the bath for an hour or two; and they should not sleep after the wind-bath, and it must be warmed when it is necessary to treat it by wind-bath, and when it has been wind-bathed.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And guard those who are healing from being coleric, and their heat is too sharp and inflamed; it is convenient that he drink cold things, such as pomes, endives, lettuce, and similar foods; and let him drink a little water, and eat little meat; and when he has wind, he should drink more than he eats; and it is convenient to give some men three times a day bitter or musk before or after ventilation, in order to strengthen the principal members; and make his stomach subtle, but it is not convenient that those who are cold should drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The suction cups that are used to cause pain are those placed on the liver, and the mouse, and podagre, and on the belly and the bowels and the rain and the hainche; because this member does not feel pain when it is cut, and we only do this to draw blood from one member to another, as we put suction cups on the mammary glands when the child is not yet born; to remove the viscous substance that is in the member, as we put suction cups on the belly and the bowels to weaken the member; and it removes pain, when there is an operation or a stone, if it is removed by its attracting virtue, or deserts the stone from its place; and so does it when it is placed on the liver and the mouse when there is wind retention, and these suction cups are emptied together to suck only a little; and they are never emptied all at once, and they are never plain with fresh water, as in the pleurisy, and in this way the suction cup is filled with hot water or water in which herbs have been boiled suitable for that.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the suction cup administered to fire is thus:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	The shape of the suction cup administered to fire is thus: It should be two hands wide and half a palm deep, and have an opening at the center just big enough for a pin or needle, as if to hold a thread, and made of brass or iron so that it does not hurt the patient when placed on the limb; and in the middle a cross bar of brass or iron, so that a grip can be taken with it; and there should be large and small ones according to the disease and age of those who take them; for the suction cups of children are different from those of old people, and those of thin people are different from those of fat people.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And it should be placed thus on the limb: Take the thread or thread grip, and put it behind the bar at the middle of the suction cup, so that the brightness is at the bottom of the suction cup so that it does not burn the patient; and then put it on the limb, and your two hands are behind the opening that we have said, so that when you put it on, if vapor comes out, and then remove the suction cup; and take the thread as before, and renew it often, if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the ventouse now which is amined in disease of pleurisy, to all water, has no verges nor perforations, and is amined only when it is plain of water, and is placed on the limb so much only; and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	In the suction cups now which are used in disease of pleurisy, to all water, have no vertices nor perforations, and are used only when they are plain of water, and are placed on the limb so much only; and this is the form: Suction cups are not used except in limbs where one cannot place suction cups due to their smallness, as lips and gums, and similar things; and in a char's leather, if a dog or deer, and others like them; and the quality of using them is that when you find suction cups which are in clear sweet water without danger, then take them; and put them into sweet water, as long as they are familiar with it, and have nothing in their bellies; and then let them go down from the vein and from the suction cup, then rub the limb until it is red, and put the suction cups on; and when they will be plain, and will be filled, if it is possible to place a suction cup there, then put it, for that is worth more afterward.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, then raise the joint from there, and then of water, very well, and then squeeze it; and if the joint is too late after the heart of the blood vessels, so moisten a linen drape in cold water, and put it on, until the blood vessels are dried up; and if the blood vessel multiplies, then put on crushed vitriole, or garlic, and similar things, until they are dried up; or you put half peeled peas on the joint, and leave them until they heat to the joint, now they will dry up; and if you need more, take other blood vessels.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	If the blood vessels do not want to take it, then rub the joint with fresh blood, or you stick an needle into it until the blood comes out, and then put them on, and sometimes when they feel the blood, they heat up; and when you see that they are peeing, then powder a little aloe and seer broached, or ash, so they will pee now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	The various chapter are often necessary in the art of medicine, and are restorative for a fracture and dislocation.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that the wise men poured this chapter on this book, which you will never find in any of the old books or letters; and for this reason the science has been lost in our land, for I have never found any good one; and I know nothing, except by the science of the old books, which I have studied so much that I have treated the science, and by experience, and by habit of my life; and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained therein, and have abridged it clearly at the end, and have shown distinctly the shapes of the instruments that are used, as I did in the two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore fitting that we begin our book with the chapters of speech and the principles where understanding is placed, and delay it on truth, so that those who are tested know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when there is a break, dislocation, twisting, or strain in anyone, it is fitting that you quickly seek to save the patient from pain on both sides, unless there is no stopping it; indeed, if it is weak of frame, or old, or its tendons are not very strong; and if he has a very small girth, or too much exercise; and does not drink cold drinks, nor eat any greasy foods, and does not fill himself with food that fills the veins with blood, until you have no doubt about the temperature of the head, or the spread of matter in the limb; then bring the patient back to his normal way of life.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary that the patient be nourished with meats which make one fat, or have viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, and rice, and eggs, and pies, and cakes of cheese, and meat, and fish fresh, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with good nutrition, the break will heal faster and sooner.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the old and decrepit broken bones cannot heal or harden the members together as they should by nature due to the age of the bone, nor do those that are too soft, such as the bones of small children; but it is necessary to fix them with large joints that hardens and joins the member together, until it hardens as it was before; and do not at all spare its work, and for this it is necessary to nourish it with large meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that the breakers are various in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the break of the head is another than the break of the foot, or of the leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all manner of breaks.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a break that goes to the knee, and another that comes with grinding, as when one cuts the hair with a razor.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a break with a wound, and a break that makes a small cut.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And to each manner there is its own tool in the restoration, according to what comes to one's mind in its place; and this is the break of the bone because it twists, and is wide open far from the joint, and is pressed by the hand; and when there is no twisting, or when it does not touch the joint, and the patient feels no great pain unless there is a fracture, but he may have twisting, or a cut, or a small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it is not necessary for you to move it by hand, but instead put on the medicine that comes next, and then gently constrain it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the fracture that it makes in the arvol, and there are the II parts separated, it is now necessary to put them together equally, so that the apostemes of a chaus come, and if the apostemes are choulz, if you leave for a day, as long as the apostemes are calmed; then he puts it equal to the mus that you can easily and carefully put on him, and know that the restoration of it is lighter than the restoration of the one who has pieces; then constrain it, as it is necessary here after.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if in the bone there are pieces broken, if the extension of the II parts is hand or foot, or at your hand if it is a small limb, or at II strings, or at a string and at your hand; and set the limb according to its natural figure, so that when the broken parts of the member are fixed, you remove by all means the additions in their places for the mus that you can, and keep that by your work there does not come to the patient injury or pain; and well join the II heads of the bones according to the best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And test well with the hand if it seems to you that it is not good: if the dressing is clean, and do not strain it too much, do not press it as those who bring it with their ovraige apophtheme hot and contraction of the member, as we have wanted many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the member is in order, teach the patient that he not move it, neither watching nor sleeping, turning or otherwise; and guard well that the member be so stable that it feel no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when there is no pain, it is not yet in order, and it is necessary to put it in a position that there be no pain; and guard well that it is put properly, so that there be no tortuosity when it is restored; and the quality of the member is according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that the broken limb is different in small size and large size and form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small limbs, as foot and hand and other members: it is convenient to wrap in linen cloth soft and fine; and those that are large, such as thigh and leg: it is convenient to wrap with a broad and hard cord, for the wide cords embrace all the limb fully, and constrain it evenly on all sides, so that there is no gap; then tighten the ligature lightly, III times or IV according to the limb, and constrict the hand a little on all the cord, then go up over the break and constrict less, so that the break is slightly removed from the break; and soften the cord slightly and slightly, until you press a great deal of blood out of the place of the break, then take another cord, and tie again tightly over the broken part; then go back to the part of the break, and constrain it lightly, not too hard or too lightly, as we said in the first line above; then put between the ligatures of linen or cloth, so that they are all even, then lie all over with a bandage, and then put your well-made splints on, if there is an abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is an abscess or an abscess, put something soothing over it, and let it rest for a few days; then tie it up with half a wide cloth wrapped in strips, or with a pole used to make cleats, or with palm branches, and be according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	And the stake that is placed over the break should be a little thicker and wider than the others; and it should also be as far away from the member as possible, small or large; then tie it up on the stakes as you did with the first one, and tie a string of the same material, like the first one; the string should be tighter, not too loose or too tight, and made of linen; for if the string is thick, like those used by foolish craftsmen who make their braces from linen threads, it is a great mistake, because the bracer cannot be equal if it is too narrow, and it only comes from one side every two inches.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is pregnant by the chaps of stars after extraction in her own limbs, then put them in sheaths of linen or another rag so that he does not bleed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the bruise, and the seam is broken, I will tell the cure here after.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it does not fit to extract stars from all the broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limbs are large, it does not fit to put stars on them before five days or seven, or more according to the urgency of the abscess, hot sometimes; and know the ancient method of plastering to restore fracture, dislocation and torsion: and that you take flour so it stands on the walls of the mill, and mix it with plenty of egg, and put this mixture, not too thin nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common way of the plasterer restoring fracture in many dispositions, and most especially in women and small children, for it is not too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way to apply plaster: for fractures, dislocations, and torsions: take the resin of the mastic tree, and the resin of the myrrh tree, and the resin of the ash tree, and safetida, and arabic gum, and mugwort; 500 pounds of each. Take myrrh and aloe, 400 pounds of each. Take alchelli, 800 pounds. And then grind them into powder and mix them with honey from bees; the patient's body heat will act as a catalyst for this plaster, because it is a good composition, and quickly heals broken bones, and benefits many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another way to apply plaster for twists: take mugwort and bee balm, 500 pounds of each; myrrh and aloe, 400 pounds of each; alchelli, 800 pounds. Grind them well and mix with honey or bee's brood; administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another way to set joints and bones out of place, to relieve the pain as soon as possible, and the sawing of the bone, and breaking it: take another new one, and softens it with boiling water and oil, and put on his place.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Emplasters of this kind do not restore, but are good for relieving a hot abscess, and properly healing the bones.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way to set broken bones: take dry fig leaves and earth-pavement leaves, grind them together, and make an emplacement.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way to set the bone in place and to calm down the abscess: take the roots of the marsh-marigold, and cut them into small pieces, and boil them in water and oil.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take the roots of marsh-mallows, chamomile, violets, vesce flour, each one a part; and grind them together, and mix with wine, and apply to the members which are warm, and apply with water or brine, and thus use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way to burn the wound more strongly than the first, when the healing of the member begins.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of mullein, and seeds of flax, buckthorn, melilot, and sweet grass, and flowers of violets and chamomile, all in equal parts; then grind them up, and make a poultice with salt water, or with sweet water, or with wine, depending on the heat of the member and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In his book he says that we should not put on the broken member anything other than a poultice made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says that it must neither be too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems to Galen that we should put on the broken member dry things a little warm, such as mirr and allspice and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way of plastering that is good for lesions and pain: take mugwort and goat hair, or feathers from a bird's tail, viscera, and rope, cut it into pieces of equal length, grind them, and make a plaster out of it and lay it on the wound.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then take off the plaster one day later, and check that the patient feels no pain, or that his bone has not moved from its place; if pain comes to the place, or itchiness, or relaxation, or swelling, hurry up and take off the plaster now, and wrap it in a light cloth, and dip it in sea water, and lift it up until the itchiness stops, and the pain is relieved; then let it rest for an hour, and then put a dry cloth on it, wet with spring water or rose oil, and bind it with a bandage, until you are sure that the abscess is warm; and then continue to gently remove the plaster, a little at a time, and do not pull it off as hard as before; and carefully keep doing this until it is completely cured.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is swollen and painful and red, I have taken it all away, and you must apply ointment and bandage, if it recurs, as you did at first.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if it does not occur to the member at all of what we have said, if it does not become loose until after III days or IV or V or VII; and never leave it for XX days, according to what is seen, as long as the break-up comes, and approaches the joint to the chair; then restrain it more than before, and make it fatter with meat, as I said before; and if you see that it dries up more than necessary, then wet it immediately with hot water, every time you loosen it, and let it be for each third day, and pour a little water there; by this work therefore cut off the pain to the member, and break down carefully what is wrong, that restore the member wrongly: it is painful, and if it comes with worry and fear, and I do not see any other thing than making it loose and doing it correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of the various ways to break
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».
