There are many ways to break [an bone], and various shapes, and the causes are distinct; because there is a fracture that is made from the impact of an axe, and the collarbone completely breaks the bone, just as it does with the haunch or buttock; and for this reason this way of breaking [an bone] is called "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Or an axe breaks the bone from above without piercing, and it is called this way of breaking  [an bone] "absolute"; and is the wound of these two great fractures or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is impact from within, or a crack, or the collarbone of stone, or falling on stone, or similar.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a penetrating fracture that approaches the membrane that is behind the bone, or that is on the bone, and this wound is great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound that has penetrated the bone is as fine as a hair, and for this reason it is called "capillaire"; and if the wound is made by a stone or by a fall or by another similar thing, and a piece of bone goes into the hole; and the head of the bone is so shaped as the blacksmith shapes his hot iron when he puts it on the bellows; then it enters between the stones.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And if the bone at the top has become wet and soft, so that it is like the head of a child; and if all these types of fractures are broken into small pieces like the stars; and I will talk about them in their own place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all kinds of fractures by pulling them up and investigating them and by the rotten cart that is above it.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The "capillaire" appearance is caused when, when you discover the bone, and you rub it up, so that it opens the fracture black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the cure for a fracture, take care of accidents due to disease, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of bile, loss of understanding, extension, palmation, feverish ague, and hairs standing on end, and others similar in many conditions, it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a hopeful accident, and you hope for healing, begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	When the break occurs first, and it is winter, you must remove the bone before the fourteenth day at most.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is summer, you must remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue around the bone does not rot, and the accident we have mentioned occurs.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the fracture of the bone occurs only as far as the tissue that covers the skull, you must split it open in this way: and this is how you should press on the chief of the patient's pain, uncover it all over the bone as well as you can, and on the shape of the wound more slowly than you can, and let decorrement of blood come to uncover the bone, or abscesses, assist him who is appropriate, and it is that you fill the space with damp fabrics in oil; and let rest the wound as long as the abscesses are calmed, then begin to remove the bone, and this is done according to II ways: one way is that you chop off narrowly in front, and this is the form.
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I pour another such amount as the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is that you have several different lengths, some short and others long, and they are pointed and made of iron; and in doing so lightly, that you do not bruise the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and tough, it is necessary that you pierce it from within, so that you send taillemens through all sides of the test, but not perfectly so as to pierce beyond the bone's edge; and there are several, so that each comes at the end of the bone's edge, so that you have taillemens for all sides; and this is the shape of the three ways of making the hole:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	And the quality for piercing inside the bone is that you put the tarele on top of the bone, and turn it with your two hands until you know that the bone has been pierced; then place the tarele somewhere else a little further along, and do so all around, then make the incisions at a slight angle as we have said, so lightly as we have mentioned, so that when you take the bone in your hand, or hold it to any of the instruments that you have there like pliers, pincers; and be careful not to touch the cerebral bone nor the sinew.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced the bone and treated it, if it is perceived that you must hold back the aprite which is held back by the bone from all other instruments similar to an incisor, but it is necessary that it be softer and more delicate than the other incisor; and if it does not hold back any small bones or scales, if it holds the bone lightly against the instrument; then heal the wound with the tenes and oignons we have mentioned.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other way to treat it is that which Galen says, which is safer; and press it very hard, for that is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is first necessary that you uncover a part of the bone, where the break is open, so that when you have uncovered this part, you shall place the tip of this lens-shaped incisor thereon, from whence it takes its form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side, and the part of the bone in two sides so that the cuts are towards the bone; then hit with a small mallet above, so that you gently break the bone all around, and take good care of the ligament that is torn; if it rubs against the bone, then gently break the bone because the bone can do great harm, and there is no fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone does not break all the way through the skin, and the bone is cut so little from above, and there are small pieces, then cover them with a sharp razor, where you must have different amounts, to adjust in each case according to its need, depending on the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you have sharp razors that are too large, then switch to smaller ones, and do not stop doing this until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other haircuts and delicate cuts, you should bring it according to its shape; and this is not something that has been answered by those who have put their studies in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the wound is covered, then you should bring a linen cloth according to the size of the wound, and moisten it with oil, and put it on the wound; then take another cloth doubled up in II or III, moisten it with wine and oil, and put it on the first cloth; and do this more lightly than you can, so that you don't injure the wound, then apply a second one above, and don't strip it off except to wash the wound completely; and let it rest for a day or two until the abscesses are calmed, thenstrip it off, and apply medicines as roots, flour of times, powder of incense, and aromatix (an unidentified substance), and similar things; and from these things make a powder, and put it on the wound, and apply medicine constantly without stinginess; and guard against leaving the wound dirty, or letting bowels gather above the cloth, for when bows gather over the linen of the skullcap, if they run and get corroded, they bring great harm to the patient; because when you put something venomous on a wound, it stings from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	If it is a bad accident that comes upon the patient, so as we have said, if there is doubt without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if black bile comes upon the patient due only to the medicine that has been put on him, whose virtue it is, then you must squeeze a part of honey and III parts of rose oil and III drapels of glue and apply it to his skin; then he should be treated in the manner in which he needs to be cured until he is well.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	You know that neither of the two bones above it ever breaks, or if one does so by itself, for these are two bones; and this bone is cartilaginous and never breaks unless it is bent or twisted and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two bones is broken, then you must push your little finger or pertuse dou neis and make an equal break in it with your index finger and at the knuckle opposite, until the bone regains its natural form; and do this lightly, and take care that the patient does not feel pain because of your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if he breaks in the upper part of the neck, and cannot come to his place, if you think that you should put it equal to the top of a thin ray.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if he breaks in two parts, then do the other way, and hurry to restore the first day if you can; if not, after the seventh or ninth, when the abscess is calm, then bandage the neck with linen strips at the top of the break. If the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you bandage another from the other side, if he breaks; and may the strips be so thick that they fill the openings of the neck.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And say that one should not dry the bandages; let each one be moistened every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem good to me, but it is necessary that they are moistened in a mixture of alum and powder of marble; then leave the bandage, until the bone is hard and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And no longer bottle up or nease peens of goose in the tent, and if there is wind to wrap it, and hold the rupture, and blow on the sick person; or do so as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if the abscesses come to a birth while you are operating, so that you put cotton wool soaked in oil or in eye drops, or in a small cup of salves.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the abscesses do not come to birth, so apply a paste from flour and sisham, and powder of incense, mixed with olive oil or with egg yolk, then put it on light poultices, and do not bind the loins; and if the break is small, and he is broken into small pieces, then extract them with suitable instruments according to this, then cut it off, and heal things that have been burned, and suddenly, as you apply pastes and oils appropriate to this; and if there is no wound within the loins, then heal the tent, and put plasters of cloth, until he is well.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the rupture of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is broken and there is no wound, and the break is small, it is not broken into two pieces, but rather a little bent inside, unless the fracture is very slight.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the break is in the right side of the jaw, you should insert your index finger into the mouth of the patient; and if the break is on the left side of the jaw, insert your index finger from the right hand, and push the break inside slightly, and make it even with the left hand as well.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break in the jaw is in two places, you should extend it on both sides until they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if there is movement in the teeth due to the break, then tie them together with a gold, silver, or silk thread; then place the broken jaw on a double cloth, and place a long, wide piece of leather over it that matches the shape of the jaw, and fasten it to the mandible with a knot, and command the patient to rest, and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the figure has changed, if you leave it for a third day, and then put back what has changed; and apply plasters, of flour from the mill with much yolk or flour from seed, after you have taken out the cerote; and put on another light plaster, and if the plasters stick, and the disposition of the sick person does not change, leave it as long as it is well; many times are healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if the abscesses come out, if you administer what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and a wound together, do not take a piece of the bone out; if subtle tools are suitable for this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is tight, if you widen it with fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have broken all these bones, and there is no delay, if the wound is large, put on it plasters suitable for this, to prevent infection, until it is healed.
de la forcele	forcibly
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	and then forces it several times in front of the shoulder, and the fracture is as follows: or it is broken and dislocated in two, and there are pieces, and it is the lighter to restore; or there is a fracture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work as follows if the fracture is without a wound, that you have two ministers, so that one holds the shoulder joint that is forced; and the others extend the neck towards the affected area; then make the fracture even on both sides, so that the shape is as it should be, and there is no appearance or hair splitting.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you have to do more, so tie the shoulder of the patient with a round staff of cloth or linen and make it large according to your need; and put out and lift up the force, and hold the staff in your hand, so that you put the break even as is appropriate.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the staff at the end, so that it comes out completely, then let the patient lie down on his back, and tie the shoulder to one side, and hold the member up with a strap, so that the bone of the staff is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then put the break on both sides, and if you find debris, so split it; and pull the pieces gently, and if the bone cannot be joined by any means, so that you take off this instrument, to save the life of the sick person:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and appears like a spoon, and is not hair, and is also as wide as it should be, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; and has II chaps, if you see, and one is wide, and the other is narrow, so as the rupture of the wound that you made when you broke the bones; and when you are sure of the aposteme being hot, if the wound is hot, and the rupture is small, or you doubt about the aposteme being hot, if employ the wound with drapels and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if hot apostemes come, if wet a drape in oil and salt and wine, and put on it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The strenging of the bone, when it is sore plaied and sore tailed, is that you put upon the bone the plaster of the powder from the mill and of the ash of ufe, and put thereon light stapes, and put a sper of wood thereabout, if thou hast need thereof; then take a very strong band of a palm wide, then put thereon a drape double, and the plaster; then take an evil thin stel of three fingers broad and long, and wrap it about that band, so that the chief of the band be hanging down; and put the stel upon the fracture, and turn the band about the neck, and fasten the stel tightly to the bone; and the ramaine of each part, and when thou seest clearly that the stel holds not the fracture back from the bone, then thou hast need to take another band, and when thou seest that it holds the fracture in place, and that thou canst feel it move no more about the bone, so that thou keepest the band thereon, and so that thou dost not loose the stel from the bone by any accident; then let the sore man lie upon his back, and put thereon a little orler of wood about the assele, to lift up the ajutoire; if thus the fracture is strengthened by the aliging of the shoulder, where thou dost bind the arm to the neck, and if no bad accident comes thereto, then begin again the plastering, if thou seest that thou hast need thereof, and fasten it and leave it so, till it be restored; and it is restored in most cases in XXVIII days, and in less time at some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	For if the shoulder dislocates and moves from its place, and does not return by itself, but returns with some effort, and then returns to its place, and is positioned correctly in all ways that you can; then put powder from the mill with much flour, and make light dustings, and put it on a double drape; then put on a wide and thin board, slightly wider than the shoulder, and tighten the board around the shoulder, so that the board does not move from its place, and keep an eye on it every day; and whenever it amoles, tighten it again, and make the board equal if it has moved away from its place, and lay the patient down on their side; and the shoulder is reset in 20 or 25 days. And when that number is complete, then let it go, and be sure, for this is not bone that moves easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone is stretched out ahead, and there is no pain in it, if done so, and the bone, and do as we have said in the breaking of the shoulder blade to calm down an abscess, warm.
de la brisure dou pis	of the breaking of the piece
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The piece is never broken in the middle, but it happens sometimes; but it often breaks at the end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, if it declines towards the joint, and the patient feels great pain, and there is no relief, and sometimes vomits blood, and opens the veins in the broken bone, and he feels all well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies down on his back, and you put a cushion between his shoulders, then press the shoulders together, and assemble the ribs of the two ribs with your hands, and gently make it even in all ways as you can, until the shape of the bone is like this; then wrap it in a cloth, and stick it on the broken bone, so that it doesn't move; and bring the strapping around the back, and tighten it tightly, and loosen it every hour, and if it relaxes, tighten it again; and if it comes to loose, because of corrosion or itching that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, then hurry, and loose it, and remove the plaster, and treat it in a way like this; then put back the plaster, and tighten it until it is well.
de la brisure des costes	of the break of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	I know that the rib fracture only occurs in large size after the spine, and towards the top, and they do not ache much unless they are bent.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the healing is such that you make the break even, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then put on plaster, and a splint of a stick if you need one.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the rib fracture is downward-facing, then the patient feels great pain and vomiting, as though he were crying; because the bone does not close the opening. And it causes great loss of strength, and it was a long time before he recovered.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if any of these serve to inflate the abdomen so that the break goes away on its own:
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make this, except for heated abscesses; if it has not come, it will come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, then let it be healed.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And no one will say that we put vacuums on the joint to suck out a form, and this seems reasonable; nevertheless, there is doubt that the vacuum does not attract the excesses to the joint due to weakness of disposition.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And no one will say that we cover the joint with another moist oil; and we put tents between the ribs to make the place even, then let it be cured with the cure for plague, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain so that he cannot endure it when the bone rubs against the tent, there is doubt in the patient; then you must split the bone at the break of the rib, and place a tool to hold it back; and then you should cut the two ends of the wound, if it is large, and treat it with poultices until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses come, then put on drapes soaked in oil and place them on the wound; and cure while the infection is in the root of the abscess, and give soothing poultices to the coast where it is, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the break of the throat
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Any time comes to the breaking of the bone of the throat, and it does not stop; and also at the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this has happened to anyone, and you can see if he will be healed or not, then take warning if your hands are swollen and inflamed and dead, and cannot move them or extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, if they do not hurt.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is fatal in many cases, and if they do not move and do not feel pain when they are held and do not hurt, know that the joint of the bone has been saved, and the patient is healed, if you put the cure on it.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if these similar things come to the spine of the back, and you do not know whether it is healthy or not, pay attention to whether its tendons are relaxed, and to the accident that caused it, whether it is in the hands, and on the back there is windiness and excretion without will; and when it has been treated with a poultice on its stomach, if there is excretion without will.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it is treated with a poultice on its back and it becomes hard, then it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that it is deadly: do not work at all in its treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come to him, then it is the lightest thing.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you treat him if there is an abscess, put oil or lard on the spine or on the back, as long as it is soothed; then put on one of the plasters that confort and dry, and tie it with a string, and order the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that side where he feels pain, until it is healthy.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if some bone is separated, cover it with wool; then tie the bone, and join the two lips of the wound, if it is large, with a stitch, then treat it with ointment, carrying it away with a cart, until it is healed; and if the bone is broken, which is called "bone of the cow", if you have a pouch, put it in your left hand, and make it equal to the other hand at your power, then apply the plaster and wood to it, if you need it; then tie it up, and if there are any bones that have been separated, press them together, and cure the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the break in the leg
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	May there be a slight break in the leg, and if so, let it not go beyond a little shortening of the bone; and make it long and level with the hip, and let it come to the patient's pain, and swelling, and let the broken part heal.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the reset so is that you extend your hand over it as long as you are above the break; and know what is the break and its shape; and if the break is at the top joint, so make that break even as long as it is in a natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is long, or it leans inward, so make the sick person sit up on his stomach, as long as the reset of that break is arranged for you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have made it even, if you put on the plaster, then put on a piece of wood or a beam, and reset the break so that it does not move; and fix the joint of the sides as even as possible.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And order the sick person to sleep on his side or back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an abscess comes out, do not scratch it, as long as the abscess is calmed down, and put on what we have mentioned above; and then return to the reset, and hold it as it should be, unless there is a bad accident; and this is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	of the dislocation of the shoulder

And if the abscesses come, do not hold back on the extraction for more than seven days, and put a moist poultice on it quickly with rose oil, until the abscesses are calmed; then extract them, and the way to extract them is that you put the plaster on the rupture, then raise the arm on the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the back; and wrap the bandage around it, and extract it above the joint, and on the arm, so that the arm remains in a good position, without any obstacle to it, or if the bone is not broken.

And if you doubt that the nose does not move, if you use props, and put on the break a prop wider and stronger than the others, and keep between each prop two spaces, and make each prop so large that it passes three times through the fracture; then strain onto the props, as I said at the beginning of the chapter on the paste on the fracture, stronger and less by moving away.

de la brisure du bras	of the fracture of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "scapula" and the "humerus," with the former being smaller and located at the front of the shoulder, and the latter being larger and positioned behind it; occasionally, one of these bones may break on its own, or both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the smaller bone is broken, restoration is easy and healing follows; but when the larger one is broken, it is a more difficult case of healing, and worse than when both are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If only the smaller bone is broken, it is necessary to gently extend it and make it even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	If only the larger bone is broken, it is necessary to more forcefully extend it; place it on one knee, and tilt the arm toward the body using the forearm as support, with the palm facing outward; the patient should cross his other arm across his body, and a helper should use their forearm to support the extended arm, with the palm facing inward. A second assistant should then support the patient's other arm at the elbow, and another person should hold the patient's opposite leg, pulling it slightly forward and upward.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then make the wound equal, according to its best shape.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it is broken into pieces, each one be placed in its place, and if any of them are loose so that they do not hold the cure, and you cannot put it back in its place, then do this to the bone as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the break there is a wound, I have spoken about it in the singular chapter; take care of the cure.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if in the restoration there come pustules that are hard, I will cover them with a cloth made of rosin oil and white wax, which is neither too hard nor too soft; and I will cover it from above gently, until the hard pustules are softened.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then remove the cerottle from the bone and put on the plaster of the powder mill with plenty of resin, because I will put on the splints, and let the splint of the break be closer together than others, and farther apart if the break is in one or two bones; and stretch it up higher than any other part, and always less by moving away, as I said at the beginning of the chapter of the ink; and may the cloth that is on the break be soft and wet, and not too hard or rough; and may the thread from which it is stretched be made of linen, neither too thick nor too fine, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And treat the limb and the lien for a few days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if some bad accident comes to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, let it be soaked with lukewarm water until the itch is relieved; and let the limb not be tightly wrapped up to rest.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then start again the extraction, and if the ligature is soft and the bone is exposed, and similar things, let it be done with care.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the limb cannot be bent, because it is too tight, let it be loosened a little and left for a few days until the stiffness passes, and then extract it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said comes to the patient, let him not be dislocated for up to 20 days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus. de la brisure de la main	In cases of hand fractures, the hands should be held close to the neck, with the wrists kept even and immobile, and they should sleep on their backs. Know that this fracture can heal in 30 or 35 days, and perhaps in 20 days, depending on the properties and complexions of the virtues.
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that at the back of the hand, and between the two hands, there are often cracks, and it only comes to a few.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is broken or split, so that the patient suffers a severe pain, and sits upright properly and evenly; then he places his hand on an extended towel, and extends the broken bones, and joins them together, making sure they are well joined; then he applies plaster and splints, if there is no abscess, then put a bandage according to the quantity of the place; and it should be wrapped in I drapery of linen.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if it breaks within the پارتن between the navel of the plant, then make a spear of drapels, and instruct the patient that he strangle his broken plant with his mouth; and then extract it with a long drapeil, and let it be as large as the plant of the hand, and extract it, as it is appropriate.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if it breaks at the end, then it is appropriate that you put a stake on it, and another deso in the plant, so that the hands are open and straight, then tie it tightly around the hand, and stop the flow between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the break comes to any of the two, it is appropriate that you make it even, as it is appropriate; and extract it with the plant, and if you see that you have to put a small straight stake to raise the break, so that it does not move; and if the break is at the other two, as in the index or one of the others, make it even, and tie it to the healthy one that comes after; or you tie them all together, that it moves, or you put a stake on it, as if you throw it; and take care in the restoration and arrangement of the aposteme heat, and help those who come to it, as I said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the chest breeze
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The ribs of the chest are sometimes bruised, and we can clearly see when they turn before and behind; and the restoration is thus: if one ties them together above the bruise, and another under it.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the sick person lies down on his face; then each minister lays his bandage evenly on his part; and that is when the break occurs in the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is near the root of the chest, then one of the bindings goes towards the knuckle, and the other binds under the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if it is near the kneecap, and then one of the bindings goes towards the kneecap, and the other under the break; then put the bone back in its natural position with his two hands, and then apply plaster and wrap it up, so that the incision comes out clean.

And if there is an abscess, so he leaves it to soothe then return to your work and your cure; the time is done in some way.

And if it falls, and turns away from what it came to, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of the bone that hold on, let them be pulled hard; and if they cannot be pulled, let the place be split and pulled out firmly; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed.

de la ruelle dou genoil	from the corner of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the corner of the knee there is little breaking, but it bleeds many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, there is only a split or a hole, and comes to all the pain, and this hurts less.
