de la brisure de la jambe	From the break of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Sache that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is called "mustelz" and the other "foscile"; it happens to them as to the arm, and for this reason the restoration is the same for both; the wounds are also all the same. And if the two bones break together, the leg turns in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if his nose is fragile, turn back.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, then one will feel great pain and see it well; and turn away.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And then bring out the limb, and make it even, and tie the joints evenly; but nevertheless, it is necessary that his fracture be ugly, and there are many pieces, so that the extension be smaller and lighter; and make it even according to your art.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have finished your work, take two long branches of fir tree that purple the leg on one side and the other, and are long from the ankle to the tip of the leg; then wrap them around it above and below, and tie it tightly in the middle, so that the leg does not lean to the right or the left, and so is good; and no one should administer a bers out of the long leg, and if it is fir, and put the leg to keep from moving, and properly make one in the fracture where there is a wound; and move each day the leg to see if there is an abscess or any other accident; then cure until it is healthy.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the break of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no break, but at the foot there is a break in some cases and not in others, and it has only broken in many cases of disposition.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a break at the foot, and you see these bones come together, so that the person puts his foot on the ground like this, as if he wants to walk; then now place your foot on its side, let those bones rise again, then press them until they return to their places; then apply plaster and put it on, and put a small board under the heel of the foot, then tie him up with bandages, and other things that you need.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three days or four have passed, if the swelling goes down, for you will find that the bones are even, whether they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are any two broken, if they are restored, as we said to the two of the hand; then put on one of the broken a stone according to its length from the two, and let it be a little wider, then tie the wet that I said, and strain it forward; and if there are II or III or more, broken, then put on each two a stone according to its quantity, wrapped in I linena cloth, and strain the wet out of the foot; and being on top of the head of the wet is far from the belly of the foot, so that he well color.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And it is necessary that you do not forget the other things that I have said to the other breakers, since we have said; and take care of each accident as it happens.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the bone of the hand
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the woman's nature is bruised, if she is seated enlarged, then lean her to the back part of the buttocks and hold her there behind; then fill the vase with the disease of cotton, and put in it as big as I stand; then undress the woman, and turn her back little by little, and then jump the cotton, until it comes to the entry of nature, and returns the bone with the back; and when she urinates, if she jumps the cotton, and when she has urinated, put it back, and so do for seven days or more: then will be restored the bruise, and she will see, take a bladder of lamb, and tie a cord to the pubis, and pour all the bladder into nature; then blow in the cord forming, until the bladder is gone inside: nature will then return the bruise; then fill it with cotton, and leave it like that for some days, until it is well.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the jaw of man or woman is broken, if it be mended as we have said in the hip bone; and these fractures are not hidden from him who puts his study and use to it, and hears my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the fracture means many things about the right way of restoration: hear then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the neck, when it is broken, take an goose's throat and put it on the neck; then wrap up a cloth around it, and let it be for three days or more, and it will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the one who has a fracture with a wound, even if it is great, as in the hip bone or shoulder or other limb, to be healed now, so that the wounds which we have spoken of bear witness to this.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals well, if the vinager remains, then you should start to restore the broken part in that same hour, or on the day when the blisters do not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if the blisters come, and you leave it to restore only until the next day, as long as the blisters are calm and not touched again in three days or four, for you would bring about a bad accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is visible above the skin, then it is necessary that you put it in place lightly with your hands, at small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extensions are not equal to your hands in length, then take this instrument made of iron, which has seven or eight lengths, and whose width is determined by the quantity of the wound; and for this one is used to the hand that it grasps three or four, according to what it requires in each cure of a broken part; and be round and a little thick, so that it does not press on the member at your work, and be sharp in front and thick from the middle onwards, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palanche," for it is necessary that the shoulder blade be placed on top of the head of the bone; and it is to be bent once, until it returns, and even one against the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is small, and the instrument cannot take hold of the bone well, then you must chop off the head of the bone until the instrument has power over it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring back the bone as we have said, with a suitable instrument, either an incision or a saw, within your power; then remove that which is remaining in the bone by roughness and small scrapings.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone has been reset, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural position.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you do so that it is in its natural position, then dip the dressing in black vinegar and apply it properly; and do not put on cotton or any other oil there, lest it bring about pus and corruption; and administer the poultices when you have reset the bone, leaving the wound uncovered, and wrap the covering all around it, according to the quantity of the wound, and be sure that the wound is not strained with the fracture; and many times this has been done to the patient, and has brought about death or corruption in no instance; and the instruments for breaking are softer and more pliable than for other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is big or bad, and you doubt that a worse accident will not come, as we have said, and you feel pain at the site, it is not right to put splints on; but wrap it up tightly, in place of splints, with hard drape, and bind it.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days a bow to the wound, if the bone that you have put on comes off entirely, and apply a healing ointment to the wound, if healing ointment with four-fold action and similar things.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you dislocate the limb twice a day, in the morning and at evening, until it is fixed and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limbs be out of joint in such a way that the bone moves down leicht.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if every day passes, and it cannot be fixed but comes off again, knowing that there are small pieces of bone that bring about the pain, then you must cut the wound with a knife, and remove all these unhappy pieces that cause the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if there is a fistula or another type of corruption, you must treat it according to what was said in the chapter on the paste mentioned above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And if the bone is broken and opened up on the member, as in the case of the hip or shoulder bone, or other large bones, do not pull it out, for many times death results, but leave it so that it may rot; perhaps after XX days or XXX, then treat the wound, if you can; and if you cannot, then leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of the rust that comes from iron
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	come to us many times after the health of the breaker, especially when it is near the joint, and it is an ugly thing to see the figure of the limb; and perhaps cannot make the limbs move naturally.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care, therefore, if we are fresh: give them stinking medicines, as balm, incense, myrrh, and sarc콜, acacia, and similar ones; so that you do not apply any of these things, or all together, and confound them with wine, or with a lot of vinegar, or with ash; and put them on the lump, and tighten it well, and do not release it for many days; and then loosen it, and start another, until the nodules are hard; or you hold it to a sharp razor; because the property of the soap is that it hardens all the swellings on the limbs; and if the nodule has turned hard like stone, it needs to be cut out, if there is an excess, and let it dry, or you will not cure it.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	the member which is weak after rest
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is healed, and there remains after weak and slender members, for diverse reasons: because one is too tightly tied, and was not tied as it should have been; or because he has too many ligaments, and cannot come into contact with the member; or because of many swellings; or because of great movements, not in his time; or because he has little blood in his body, so he is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and make his body soft, until the blood multiplies in him; and give him baths, and offer him pleasure and exercise; then put resin on the member, so that the resin attracts great nutrition, and drenches it often with warm water, until the nutrition flows to the member; and return it to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	two tortured limbs after sickness
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limbs are twisted after recovery, and the bone is broken open, and the form of the limb is ugly, however it does not lose its natural function: do not believe the foolish who say that you must break a member all over again, and many fools have done this in our land; these practices are blamed, and great harm and sometimes death result; nevertheless, if the nodules and torments are fresh, they should be soaked in warm water or cooked herbs are used, as foils of walleye, roots, and melilote, and similar things; and the salve should be softened with a good oil, such as dyaquillon well made, and you take the muskellunge of walleye, and confound it with sheep's fat or sesame oil, and make a poultice; or you take figs, and crush them with hay of corn, and similar medicines that soften the pain.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And there is no time when the shoulder is dislocated by constantly and repeatedly rubbing with damp hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let there be no movement in the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the limb is twisted and hardens like stone, it must be opened with a sharp tool lightly, and covering the bone, and making a cut, and putting vinegar and studying in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations:
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to anyone, if it is now brought back by gentle movement.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if we delay, and the joints grow larger, and by chance do we reset to its place; because then it cannot be moved at all: many times this causes pain and other pains; but when this will come, if you make the patient well, then leave him, until the abscess is calmed down; then raise the limb with warm water and oil, then move it slightly, and cure each limb as the cure comes to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the ointments for dislocations of the shoulder joint until the tip.
des mandibules	of the mandible
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Now it has happened that the mandibules have dislocated and they are in two ways: where they are a little out of place and stiff a little; or they are completely dislocated, and hang down to the chest, and cut off the salive from the mouth so that he cannot hold it, nor can he close his mouth, and wrap his tongue with words.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, return it by means of several movements.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is complete and accomplished, then you must quickly reset it in the hospital, and do not delay at all; and in this way that the ministers hold the head of the sick person, and pour a little ointment from one of his hands into the root of the dislocation of the mandible inside the mouth, there are two parts to the dislocation; and the other two hands should be away, to make it even; and order the patient that his mandibules be softened, and moved in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And let the mirror be equal, until it revives in its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And let them be brought back gently, even if both mandibles are together, but heat and oil are brought to them as soon as they are taken off, so that they are gently brought back; do not delay in bringing them back, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are gently brought back and the mouth of the sick person is closed well with a softener, place it on cloth soaked in wax made of oil and wax, then lightly move it around while it is still warm; and let the sick person sleep on their back, and their shoulders be between two pillows, so that he does not move from side to side or struggle to turn over, but rest legily, until the pains are gone and the mandibules are well healed. And then eat lightly, and do not try to open the mouth for eating or drinking, until the mandible is well healed and pain-free.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be set in place within an hour, and are not returned to their places, then fever and sudor will come of custom, and peradventure a solution from the belly, and per aventure vomiting of pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is a loss; and often dies he who has it, within nine days.
de la forcelle	of the fork
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	Does not dislodge from within the continuation of the et from the foot, and is dislocated no more than once to the side, and it feels very much.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is such that the patient lies down on his back, and extends his arms; and then press the joint with your palm, and it will come back; then put on the plaster and bandage, and bind it; and the jaw which is towards his chest cannot dislocate; if not, and if it dislocates no more than once, then you return it to its place, as we have said; then put on the plaster and the bandage, and bind it, and command to the patient that he rest until he is well; and so also is the head of the shoulder returned when dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Saiches that the shoulder can dislocate in three ways: either because one of its parts comes out of place with respect to the other; and the second is at the base of the arm; and sometimes it dislocates upward, which happens little; and it never dislocates behind or inside; and many times it dislocates forward towards the shoulder, but in those who have a little cart, because it will need to be hospitalized; and in those who have enough cart, it is not necessary to do anything, and return to their homes.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes there are homes where they hit or break it, and the shoulder inflames with heat, and one thinks that it has dislocated because of that.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	So then you must test it, until you are sure of it; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And there comes the dislocations when it is swallowed into the axilla, and distinguish between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find between them a manifest difference; and you will find at the head of the shoulder a pit, and sever the axilla at the top of the head of the shoulder, as if it were an egg; and the patient cannot bring his hand to his nose, nor move from any movement; and also, if it is dislocated upwards, then it is not hidden, for you will find it clearly on the top; and this way of dislocation is not a reason to return, when it is new, or if the person is ill.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the way is that the ministers lift up the hand of the sick man, then put your slings off the axilla, and lift up the joint by force to the place; and the ministers lift up the hand, and extend it upward, then put it down; so comes gradually.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said in our days later, it is convenient that the patient be bathed in hot water; and give him a soothing and relaxing enema, as an infusion of althaea and fenugreek and melilote in water, and let him be sat on; then let the back of the patient be warmed with a warm cloth, not too hot or too cold, and put the stirrup over his shoulder, and gently lift the patient's arm; and give another minister to lift the patient's arm, so that it does not move; this shoulder returns all at once, and if you do it according to this way: and it is that you make present a man who is greater than the patient; and let him stand on his right side, and take the back of the patient's seat, and lift up the seat, so that the patient hangs in the air; and give another ministers to draw the patient's arm down towards his belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, without anything heavy with him, and the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And if you also do it in another way: and is it that a long stick is placed in the ground, whose head is also like a pistol, and is not too large or too small; then let the patient lie on his back on the end of the stick; then let him extend his hand on either side forming a line, and the joint will return to its place peacefully; and if it does not come back for all these things that we have said, then do this cure: take a stick from the two arms of a great tree and four fingers wide, which has the head turned by completely entering under the axletree, according to this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	then lie on the top of the stick drapelsouez, that the fust does not scarce lou malaide, then put it under the axletree; and extends som arms on the top of the long stick, and places the shoulder on the stick, and the arm at the head of the hand, then put the arm on an eschillon of a big tree, and let the hands extend downstream, and let the body hang from one side: the joint will return now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is on, in any way that it may be, it is necessary that you put upon the shoulder an equal sphere of wool, then place the plaster prepared from powder from the mill, with incense and honey of bees, over all the shoulder and back, then remove the ring from the shoulder forward, and tie the thread to the plaster, and embrace the hand at his neck, and let the hands remain in this way.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he suck a little while until the members are comfortable, for he will heal more quickly; and then suck more after 5 or 7 days, and move it; and if it is firm and has not softened, then it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint has moved out of place due to moisture or some other cause, it is necessary that you administer the cauterizations three times, as it is placed in front or with the paste of the cauterizations.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it slides after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot raise its arm upstairs, then know that the nerves in the head of the shoulder are cut or stretched or weakened; and know that the joint has never been placed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the dislocation that is towards the back of the hip, and the glutes, or behind, is made by a blow, and stretching of the hands, and I administer another place; and cure as long as it is healthy.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing comes greasiness to the member, and tardiness in movement, then the patient uses oil many times, until that greasiness is gone, and returns to its first nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the neck
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the neck is dislocated to a degree, and dislocates again; and it is dislocated from all sides, most of all in front and behind, and the dislocation is not returned, for we see it well and feel it well; and dislocates according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick shoulder with the sound one, if you can see it openly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is dislocated, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary that you reset it in the same way as the shoulder joints come out, because if they come out the way they come in, then it would be painful to set them back; and by chance it cannot be reset all at once from all sides, most especially when it is behind; so it is worse than other dislocations, and causes great pain, and by chance it leads to death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is done, when she is so that you can reset her, that you extend her hand with your two hands; and its arms are spread out, and the hands of her hand according to the sound side, forward and backward, and press the joint back into its palm roots together, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if it is dislocated in front, he returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and he feels at the root of the palm which is dislocated from the outside.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not return to its place, he ministers a strong extension; and it is that two minister extend the arm, and they color them two, so that it does not move at the extension; then turn the arm of each part, then you have wrapped a double long and wide cloth; and when you see him join the joint to his hand, then oile it of any oil to soften the joint, then press the joint firmly, until he recovers; and when it is in its place, put it on plaster dry with honey of thyme, and strain it firmly, and wrap the arm around the neck of the sick person, and leave it for some days, then release it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, then loosen it and leave it; and if you see that the joint is not well set, then recommence the plastering and binding and leave it thus for some days, until it is firmly set; then loosen it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels pain after the joint is moved and it moves, then bathe and rub well, and press until it is eased; or put on the joint a wet sheep's fur, then leave it for a day and a night, then the bone, and let it enter or swim; and when it sweats, rub the joint well, then put the fur back on, and then enter or swim; and do this II times or III, until it is healed; and if you see, then put on a wet sheep's skin heated with butter, and strain it over; then return to its position.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The dislocation of the hand is less severe than that of other joints, however it must be brought back into place carefully during the dislocation, so that the joint does not swell or that there is no abscess.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And when you bring it back, put the sick hand on a table and extend the fingers, and make them even so that they rest against the joint, and bring them back in this way; but it is necessary to watch carefully that they are placed correctly; then place the patient's hand with its back on a table for extension and retraction.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	If the dislocation is at the back of the hand, then put the patient's hand with its back on the table, and make the joint appear to the patient's eyes.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, this is good; but if not, if the extraction of the pustules that have broken out apains them, and so leaves them with a bad taste.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	If he cannot bear it, and you cannot set it to its place after several days, if the joint twists; and there is no benefit to the patient without breaking the nerves or arteries: then you know that the nerve are cut, or the arteries; so you must extract it by a delicate cautery, and perhaps there is nothing else to be done.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, if you put on the poultice that we have said, then extract it and leave it for 5 days, then remove it and leave it again.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	If he cannot move it well, and there is no fracture, if he dips it in hot water, and rubs it until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the two fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	of the dislocation of the two fingers of the hand are not dislocated to each side, not on the back of the palm or the belly; so they are, and pull the dislocation to your knuckles until it comes back, then support the head of the finger with your thumb, and turn it towards the part where it is joined; and leave it there for a day, and then put it back even that day; and from nut, if he has been dislocated on the belly of the hand, do so often as it is stiff, and all as you have done before, until it is healed; and do the same, when it is dislocated on the other side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	of the dislocation of the shoulder at the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the shoulder or neck is dislocated, or there are several dislocations, there is no cure, for it kills the patient quickly.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens Whisthleb, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee "gilbositez": li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And those that come from falling or strikes or similar things, the ancient ways of cure with great words, which did not bring much good; but I have shortened it according to my intention, and have formed tools in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the Gilbosity that comes from behind, one does not have to cure or heal; and also those that come straight on both sides, and can only be cured properly who comes from behind, as I said; it is that the sick person be extended on his face in an equal position, and has a strain of it, so that he does not bleed; then lay one ember on the head forming a ground, and another to the feet, and tie a string to the back of the sick, and another to the ankles, and two ministers know the strings, one at the head and the other to the feet, among the two embers; and let them be well closed, the ember as we have said before, and the mirior puts his palms on the spine forming, until he recovers.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return with this cure, then take a bowl of three arms long, and cover the wall, and let the patient be on the side, and pour the head of the bowl over the wall, then put the middle of the bowl on the spine; and place the tips of his fingers on the other head of the bowl, and press firmly until it returns to its place; and if you see that, do so with the knob that turns in the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And that you stick two torches to the head of the sick person with an arm long, and place the tips of the other two on top, and put a palm of space of length between each torch; and in each torch have a hole where the turner runs, and let the torch firmly into the ground so that it does not move; and between each pair of torches have one turning torch, so that the string turns, and have two small torches of a palm of length to turn the turner; and then bind the knot that is among the strings to the turner at the head, and the other knot to the tips on the other turner, and let each servant turn his torch on all the string, and the master put the spine in line as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	Et when it is even, put upon it dry plaster with much urine, and then the stakes, and then the stem of a tablet of three inches long, that purplish may take up its place in the bosom of the glutus and the part of the spine sound, and bind with a thread, as we have said, and use on the patient subtle fasting, until he is well; and if any thing comes at the end of the health, then administer medicines softening and soothing, with the stem that we have said above; and never do I administer a piece of lead, and never does the appearance come in the posterior spine of the back, and take care that it is dislocations; and this is the bone that opens, so that one must not have presumption: per adventure would bring about death.
des dislocations de la hainche	the hips
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Saiches that the joints of the hip and shoulder only come about due to dislocations, not at all like other joints; and the joint of the hip is dislocated according to IV parties: inward and outward, and before and behind; and more inward there, and less dislocated before and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of its dislocations inward is that when one joins the wounded leg with the sound, it is more distant, and the patient's knees are farther apart than those of the sound; and the patien'ts cannot double his knee in front; and it is the place that is swollen hot with an abscess, for this reason the head of the thigh comes out.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him to whom it comes outwardly is that this accident is opposite to these before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of him to whom it comes before are that his leg is well according to the accomplishment; nevertheless, he does not double his knee in pain, and when one forces him to go, he cannot walk forward, and he holds back his urine, and swells his ankle, and when he goes, he goes on the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of that person who has it behind, if he can not spread his knee, nor double it, and is that leg more twisted than the other, and the joint is softened, and the hip bone is in place between the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	And those who bring this kind of dislocation should know that if the dislocation is old and does not improve with time, there will be no cure for it; and it is only due to pride.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in those whose dislocation is new, and there are four ways of dislocation, if you hurry to reset the joint, and turn it inward and outward, and move it from side to side; perhaps it will come back into place, and there will be no need for any other cure.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not come back in this way, you must bring two strong ministers and hold the leg very firmly with them, or tie it to the ground; and let another minister extend his hand above and below in such a way that he pinches his hands together, then take him by the hip bone; and let others pull at the foot; and they should all move at once, so that the patient is raised from the ground, and remain still.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is so common to four appearances, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, then it is necessary to put the cure to its form When the dislocations are in the shoulder, then it is necessary that you support the patient on his back, then place the bandage over the root of the chest, and the bar that is away from the armpit, then extend the bandage up towards the armpit, and down towards the forceps; then pinch another minister his arms, and embrace the large bar of the chest malady, and extend it in a twist form: now it will return to its place; and this manner of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot do this way that we have said, it is necessary that you tie the two feet of the patient together with a strong bandage around the heels and knees, and let the leg be extended twice as far as the other; then hang him by the head from a pole, and have his two arms outstretched; then command another minister to embrace the root of the chest, and have other ministers hanging with the patient who embrace the chest, for the joint returns now gradually.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocations are in the other place, so he lies down the patient, as we said in that which has gibositeit, and draws out the threads properly on the bad leg, and also on the foot; then set II torches, I to the head and another to the toe, then put one torch between the legs of the patient by his side the shape; and have planted wet flagels around, so that it does not burn the patient, then extends each minister towards him, and he puts his hand equal to his dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, put him on a . table, and press him so as we have said in the gibosité, and lie down the patient on the healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocations are in front, so extend the bad leg carefully, and according to what I said; and put the patient's pain on the bad ankle, then press with the other hand, and stretch it down towards the kneecap.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocations are on the side, it is not necessary to extend the patient downward, nor to raise him up from the ground; but it is necessary that he be placed as if he were in bed with his back and legs extended as we have said above; and press down on the joint at the table; and it will be ready when the patient extends his legs, and they will be even; then spread out the knees, apply the plaster, and tie a bandage around them so that the leg does not move; and let him rest for three or four days, then remove the bandage, and cause the animal to bark loudly until the members are comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	From the dislocation of the hip joint:
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The genous are dislocated according to three manners: that is to say, inward and outward, and behind; and not in front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are that you command the patient that he bend his leg to his foot, and if it does not [bend] at his foot, take note that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and place your back on his face, and place his foot on your feet; then take his kneecap with your palms, and pull between your two hands, and bend the two sides of the knee cap in form; and other ministers extend his foot, until the genous returns to its place, and the signs are that he [bends] his leg well at his foot slightly; and apply the plaster, and make him move his leg to his foot, and fasten them together firmly for three days or four, then let him go free; and do not work on the patient to walk until his members are comfortable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limbs are not in place, give a strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the leg, until they are healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation from the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are not dislocated once and fully displaced inward and outward.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is displaced, and try again at the part where it has been displaced: We must bring it gently to our hands when it is only slightly dislocated.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is displaced all the way up, you must make the patient lie down on his back, and put the limb at rest on the ground, and then pull it gently with your hands toward you, holding it by the ankle; then try to bring the foot to you with your right hand, and then with your left two times, and then extend it upward, and blow gently on the foot; and do this twice, as we have said, in blowing and pulling the foot; if it returns, it is good; if not, restart the work, for it will return; and if it cannot return thus, you shall make the patient walk on his heels, and place the staff firmly in the ground between his knees, and tie the drape around it so that he does not fall; then put the minister on the knee, and another minister extends the foot at its rest to his hands or to the leg, that he may hold the limb; then the minister who is holding the limb makes sure that the dislocation is held in place with the drape, and other ministers pull the healthy leg forward, and the dislocation will return all the way.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it has set, then put on the plaster and press it down, and form the splint, and fasten the foot to the leg, and guard the tendons that are behind the ankle, so that the ligatures do not become too tight; then let him rest for two or three days, and the ligatures will become looser if the splint is left on; then remove the splint after three days or a quarter of a month, and let the patient walk after four days; and if he goes beyond that term, it is not yet certain that he has not dislocated again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscesses have opened, if it is necessary that you calm them down, as we have said elsewhere, until they are well.
des dois	the two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two are dislocated, if it is necessary to move them without working, and that is a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Et s'il est dislocé en aucun nu de dos de pied, si convient que tu fais asseoir le malade sus I leu plain ou sus table tot droit, et met ton pied sur ce qui aper de ces jointures, puis presse à ton pied forme tant qu'il revienne; et quand il est égal, et il n'i' aper rien, si met désoz la plante du pied une table à II chieus, puis l'estrain forme, et le laisse III jors, puis le délise; et le fais reposer, tant qu'il soit sané.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	Of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound occurs with dislocation, and one must restore it, many times the patient has died: so be not presumptuous in the cure, if you are not learned in the art and have not long practiced it, and if you are not compassionate and slow, do not be haughty; and use at the beginning soothing ointments on the hot wound, and leave the patient to God, if you see no hope of health; and when you see hope, then now restore the member to its place, so that the hot wounds come; and when the member is in its place, administer soothing ointments, and cure the wound as I have said, of dried ointments; and if with the dislocation there is a fracture, and small bones are broken, then set them, and do what we have said in simple illnesses; and guard yourself from entering the way of fear, according to what I have said, for this will cost you much according to your Creator, and for the sake of arming and healing your body.
Amen	Amen
